           </a>
          </span>
          <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/52/Sk-Slovensko.ogg" title="Sk-Slovensko.ogg">
           listen
          </a>
         </span>
        </span>
        )
       </small>
       ), officially the
       <b>
        Slovak Republic
       </b>
       (Slovak:
       <i>
        <span lang="sk">
         Slovenská republika
        </span>
       </i>
       ,
       <span class="unicode haudio">
        <span class="fn">
         <span style="white-space:nowrap">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Sk-Slovensk%C3%A1_republika.ogg" title="About this sound">
           <img alt="About this sound" data-file-height="20" data-file-width="20" height="11" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" width="11"/>
          </a>
         </span>
         <a class="internal" href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/9/96/Sk-Slovensk%C3%A1_republika.ogg" title="Sk-Slovenská republika.ogg">
          listen
         </a>
        </span>
        <small class="metadata audiolinkinfo" style="cursor:help;">
         (
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           help
          </span>
         </a>
         ·
         <a href="/wiki/File:Sk-Slovensk%C3%A1_republika.ogg" title="File:Sk-Slovenská republika.ogg">
          <span style="cursor:help;">
           info
          </span>
         </a>
         )
        </small>
       </span>
       ),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a landlocked country in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">
        Central Europe
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is bordered by the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
        Czech Republic
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">
        Austria
       </a>
       to the west,
       <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
        Poland
       </a>
       to the north,
       <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">
        Ukraine
       </a>
       to the east and
       <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">
        Hungary
       </a>
       to the south. Slovakia's territory spans about 49,000 square kilometres (19,000 sq mi) and is mostly mountainous. The population is over 5 million and comprises mostly
       <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">
        ethnic Slovaks
       </a>
       . The capital and largest city is
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
        Bratislava
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       is
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">
        Slovak
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Slavs" title="Slavs">
        Slavs
       </a>
       arrived in the territory of present-day Slovakia in the 5th and 6th centuries. In the 7th century, they played a significant role in the creation of
       <a href="/wiki/Samo%27s_Empire" title="Samo's Empire">
        Samo's Empire
       </a>
       and in the 9th century established the
       <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Nitra" title="Principality of Nitra">
        Principality of Nitra
       </a>
       . In the 10th century, the territory was integrated into the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       and the dissolution of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_Empire" title="Austro-Hungarian Empire">
        Austro-Hungarian Empire
       </a>
       , the Slovaks and Czechs established
       <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">
        Czechoslovakia
       </a>
       . A separate (First)
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%9345)" title="Slovak Republic (1939–45)">
        Slovak Republic (1939–1945)
       </a>
       existed in
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       as a
       <a href="/wiki/Client_state" title="Client state">
        client state
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       . In 1945, Czechoslovakia was re-established and under
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Czechoslovakia_(1948%E2%80%9389)" title="History of Czechoslovakia (1948–89)">
        Communist rule
       </a>
       became a
       <a href="/wiki/Satellite_state" title="Satellite state">
        Soviet satellite
       </a>
       . In 1989, the
       <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">
        Velvet Revolution
       </a>
       ended Communist rule in Czechoslovakia. Slovakia became an independent state on 1 January 1993 after the peaceful
       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">
        dissolution of Czechoslovakia
       </a>
       , sometimes known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">
        Velvet Divorce
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Slovakia is a
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">
        high-income
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Developed_country" title="Developed country">
        advanced economy
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-World_Bank_Country_Classification_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-World_Bank_Country_Classification-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with a very high
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_Human_Development_Index" title="List of countries by Human Development Index">
        Human Development Index
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HighOECD_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-HighOECD-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-qq_15-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-qq-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       a very high
       <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">
        standard of living
       </a>
       and performs favourably in measurements of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freedom_in_the_World_(report)" title="Freedom in the World (report)">
        civil liberties
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Press_Freedom_Index" title="Press Freedom Index">
        press freedom
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship_and_surveillance_by_country" title="Internet censorship and surveillance by country">
        internet freedom
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Democracy_Index" title="Democracy Index">
        democratic governance
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Global_Peace_Index" title="Global Peace Index">
        peacefulness
       </a>
       . The country maintains a combination of
       <a href="/wiki/Market_economy" title="Market economy">
        market economy
       </a>
       with a comprehensive
       <a href="/wiki/Social_security" title="Social security">
        social security
       </a>
       system. Citizens of Slovakia are provided with
       <a href="/wiki/Universal_health_care" title="Universal health care">
        universal health care
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Free_education" title="Free education">
        free education
       </a>
       and one of the longest paid
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maternity_leave" title="Maternity leave">
        maternity leave
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">
        OECD
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country joined the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       in 2004 and the
       <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">
        Eurozone
       </a>
       on 1 January 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Slovakia is also a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">
        Schengen Area
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">
        NATO
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">
        United Nations
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">
        OECD
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">
        WTO
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/CERN" title="CERN">
        CERN
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/OSCE" title="OSCE">
        OSCE
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">
        Council of Europe
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">
        Visegrád Group
       </a>
       . The Slovak economy is one of the fastest growing economies in Europe and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP_growth_rate" title="List of countries by real GDP growth rate">
        3rd fastest
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">
        eurozone
       </a>
       . Its legal tender, the
       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">
        Euro
       </a>
       , is the world's
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_exchange_market#Trading_characteristics" title="Foreign exchange market">
        2nd most traded currency
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bis.org_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-bis.org-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although regional income inequality is high,
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_home_ownership_rate" title="List of countries by home ownership rate">
        90% of citizens own their homes
       </a>
       . In 2016, Slovak citizens had visa-free or visa-on-arrival access to 165 countries and territories, ranking the Slovak passport 11th in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Slovakia is the world’s largest per-capita car producer with a total of 1,040,000 cars manufactured in the country in 2016 alone
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-touchit.sk_20-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-touchit.sk-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_motor_vehicle_production" title="List of countries by motor vehicle production">
        7th largest car producer
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       . The car industry represents 43% of Slovakia's industrial output, and a quarter of its exports.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Cuisine
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
          <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-46">
           <a href="#Sport">
            <span class="tocnumber">
             9.6
            </span>
            <span class="toctext">
             Sport
            </span>
           </a>
          </li>
         </ul>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47">
         <a href="#See_also">
          <span class="tocnumber">
           10
          </span>

          </span>
         </a>
        </li>
        <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-48">

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">
        Etymology
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The first written mention of name
       <i>
        Slovakia
       </i>
       is in 1586 (
       <a href="/wiki/German_language" title="German language">
        German
       </a>
       :
       <i>
        <span lang="de">
         In
         <a href="/wiki/Liptov" title="Liptov">
          Liptau
         </a>
         , bei der Stadt
         <a href="/wiki/Liptovsk%C3%BD_Mikul%C3%A1%C5%A1" title="Liptovský Mikuláš">
          Sankt Nikolaus
         </a>
         in der Slovakia
        </span>
       </i>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_21-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-name-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It derives from the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">
        Czech
       </a>
       word
       <i>
        Slováky
       </i>
       ; previous German forms were
       <i>
        Windischen landen
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        Windenland
       </i>
       (the 15th century).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_21-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-name-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The native name
       <i>
        Slovensko
       </i>
       (1791) derives from an older name of Slovaks
       <i>
        Sloven
       </i>
       what may indicate its origin before the 15th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-name_21-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-name-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The original meaning was geographic (not political), since Slovakia was a part of the multiethnic
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [note 1]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and did not form a separate administrative unit in this period.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="History">
        History
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">

          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">

          <b>

           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">

           </a>
          </b>

          <span class="hide-when-compact">
