      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_Slovakia" title="History of Slovakia">
        History of Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Moravianska_venusa.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="400" data-file-width="300" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Moravianska_venusa.jpg/170px-Moravianska_venusa.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6d/Moravianska_venusa.jpg/255px-Moravianska_venusa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6d/Moravianska_venusa.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Moravianska_venusa.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moravany_Venus" title="Moravany Venus">
          Venus
         </a>
         from
         <a href="/wiki/Moravany_nad_V%C3%A1hom" title="Moravany nad Váhom">
          Moravany nad Váhom
         </a>
         , which dates back to 22,800 BC
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Radiocarbon_dating" title="Radiocarbon dating">
        Radiocarbon dating
       </a>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">
          <span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (November 2016)">
           dubious
          </span>
         </a>
         <span class="metadata">
          –
          <a href="/wiki/Talk:Slovakia#Dubious" title="Talk:Slovakia">
           discuss
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       puts the oldest surviving archaeological artefacts from Slovakia – found near
       <a href="/wiki/Nov%C3%A9_Mesto_nad_V%C3%A1hom" title="Nové Mesto nad Váhom">
        Nové Mesto nad Váhom
       </a>
       – at 270,000 BC, in the
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Paleolithic" title="Lower Paleolithic">
        Early Paleolithic
       </a>
       era. These ancient tools, made by the
       <a href="/wiki/Clactonian" title="Clactonian">
        Clactonian
       </a>
       technique, bear witness to the ancient habitation of Slovakia.
      </p>
      <p>
       Other
       <a href="/wiki/Stone_tool" title="Stone tool">
        stone tools
       </a>
       from the
       <a href="/wiki/Middle_Paleolithic" title="Middle Paleolithic">
        Middle Paleolithic
       </a>
       era (200,000 – 80,000 BC) come from the Prévôt (Prepoštská) cave near
       <a href="/wiki/Bojnice" title="Bojnice">
        Bojnice
       </a>
       and from other nearby sites.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The most important discovery from that era is a
       <a href="/wiki/Neanderthal" title="Neanderthal">
        Neanderthal
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Human_skull" title="Human skull">
        cranium
       </a>
       (c. 200,000 BC), discovered near
       <a href="/wiki/G%C3%A1novce" title="Gánovce">
        Gánovce
       </a>
       , a village in northern Slovakia.
      </p>
      <p>
       Archaeologists have found prehistoric human skeletons in the region, as well as numerous objects and vestiges of the
       <a href="/wiki/Gravettian" title="Gravettian">
        Gravettian
       </a>
       culture, principally in the river valleys of
       <a href="/wiki/Nitra_(river)" title="Nitra (river)">
        Nitra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hron" title="Hron">
        Hron
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ipe%C4%BE" title="Ipeľ">
        Ipeľ
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1h" title="Váh">
        Váh
       </a>
       and as far as the city of
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDilina" title="Žilina">
        Žilina
       </a>
       , and near the foot of the
       <a href="/wiki/Vihorlat_Mountains" title="Vihorlat Mountains">
        Vihorlat
       </a>
       , Inovec, and
       <a href="/wiki/Tribe%C4%8D" title="Tribeč">
        Tribeč
       </a>
       mountains, as well as in the
       <a href="/wiki/Myjava" title="Myjava">
        Myjava
       </a>
       Mountains. The most well-known finds include the oldest female statue made of
       <a href="/wiki/Mammoth" title="Mammoth">
        mammoth
       </a>
       -bone (22,800 BC), the famous
       <a href="/wiki/Venus_of_Moravany" title="Venus of Moravany">
        Venus of Moravany
       </a>
       . The statue was found in the 1940s in
       <a href="/wiki/Moravany_nad_V%C3%A1hom" title="Moravany nad Váhom">
        Moravany nad Váhom
       </a>
       near
       <a href="/wiki/Pie%C5%A1%C5%A5any" title="Piešťany">
        Piešťany
       </a>
       . Numerous necklaces made of shells from Cypraca thermophile
       <a href="/wiki/Gastropoda" title="Gastropoda">
        gastropods
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Tertiary" title="Tertiary">
        Tertiary
       </a>
       period have come from the sites of Zákovská, Podkovice, Hubina, and Radošina. These findings provide the most ancient evidence of commercial exchanges carried out between the
       <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Sea" title="Mediterranean Sea">
        Mediterranean
       </a>
       and Central Europe.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Bronze_Age">
        Bronze Age
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Bronze Age">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Web_Biatec.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="408" data-file-width="824" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Web_Biatec.jpg/220px-Web_Biatec.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Web_Biatec.jpg/330px-Web_Biatec.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/64/Web_Biatec.jpg/440px-Web_Biatec.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Web_Biatec.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Left: a
         <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">
          Celtic
         </a>
         <a href="/wiki/Biatec" title="Biatec">
          Biatec
         </a>
         coin
         <br/>
         Right: five
         <a href="/wiki/Slovak_koruna" title="Slovak koruna">
          Slovak crowns
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">
        Bronze Age
       </a>
       in the geographical territory of modern-day Slovakia went through three stages of development, stretching from 2000 to 800 BC. Major cultural, economic, and political development can be attributed to the significant growth in production of copper, especially in central Slovakia (for example in
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0pania_Dolina" title="Špania Dolina">
        Špania Dolina
       </a>
       ) and northwest Slovakia. Copper became a stable source of prosperity for the local population.
      </p>
      <p>
       After the disappearance of the Čakany and
       <a href="/wiki/Velatice" title="Velatice">
        Velatice
       </a>
       cultures, the
       <a href="/wiki/Lusatian_culture" title="Lusatian culture">
        Lusatian
       </a>
       people expanded building of strong and complex fortifications, with the large permanent buildings and administrative centres. Excavations of Lusatian
       <a href="/wiki/Hillfort" title="Hillfort">
        hill forts
       </a>
       document the substantial development of trade and agriculture at that period. The richness and the diversity of tombs increased considerably. The inhabitants of the area manufactured arms, shields, jewellery, dishes, and statues.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Iron_Age">
        Iron Age
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Iron Age">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Hallstatt_Period">
        Hallstatt Period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Hallstatt Period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The arrival of tribes from
       <a href="/wiki/Thrace" title="Thrace">
        Thrace
       </a>
       disrupted the people of the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Kalenderberg_culture&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Kalenderberg culture (page does not exist)">
        Kalenderberg culture
       </a>
       , who lived in the hamlets located on the plain (
       <a href="/wiki/Sere%C4%8F" title="Sereď">
        Sereď
       </a>
       ) and in the hill forts like Molpír, near
       <a href="/wiki/Smolenice" title="Smolenice">
        Smolenice
       </a>
       , in the
       <a href="/wiki/Little_Carpathians" title="Little Carpathians">
        Little Carpathians
       </a>
       . During Hallstatt times, monumental burial mounds were erected in western Slovakia, with princely equipment consisting of richly decorated vessels, ornaments and decorations. The burial rites consisted entirely of cremation. The common people were buried in flat urnfield cemeteries. A special role was given to weaving and the production of textiles. The local power of the "Princes" of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hallstatt_culture" title="Hallstatt culture">
        Hallstatt period
       </a>
       disappeared in Slovakia during the last century before the middle of first millennium BCE, after strife between the
       <a href="/wiki/Scythians" title="Scythians">
        Scytho
       </a>
       -Thracian people and locals, resulting in abandonment of the old hill-forts. Relatively depopulated areas soon caught interest of emerging
       <a href="/wiki/Celts" title="Celts">
        Celtic
       </a>
       tribes, who advanced from the south towards the north, following the Slovak rivers, peacefully integrating into the remnants of the local population.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span id="La_T.C3.A8ne_Period">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="La_Tène_Period">
        La Tène Period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: La Tène Period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       From around 500 BC, the territory of modern-day Slovakia was settled by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Celt" title="Celt">
        Celts
       </a>
       , who built powerful
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Oppida" title="Oppida">
         oppida
        </a>
       </i>
       on the sites of modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
        Bratislava
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn" title="Devín">
        Devín
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Biatec" title="Biatec">
        Biatecs
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Silver_coin" title="Silver coin">
        silver coins
       </a>
       with inscriptions in the Latin alphabet, represent the first known use of writing in Slovakia. At the northern regions, remnants of the local population of Lusatian origin, together with Celtic and later Dacian influence, gave rise to the unique
       <a href="/wiki/P%C3%BAchov_culture" title="Púchov culture">
        Púchov culture
       </a>
       , with advanced crafts and iron-working, many hill-forts and fortified settlements of central type with coinage of the "Velkobysterecky" type (no inscriptions, with a horse on one side and a head on the other). This culture is often connected with the Celtic tribe mentioned in Roman sources as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cotini" title="Cotini">
        Cotini
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Roman_Period">
        Roman Period
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Roman Period">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       From 2
       <a href="/wiki/Anno_Domini" title="Anno Domini">
        AD
       </a>
       , the expanding
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">
        Roman Empire
       </a>
       established and maintained a series of outposts around and just north of the
       <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">
        Danube
       </a>
       , the largest of which were known as
       <a href="/wiki/Carnuntum" title="Carnuntum">
        Carnuntum
       </a>
       (whose remains are on the main road halfway between Vienna and Bratislava) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Brigetio" title="Brigetio">
        Brigetio
       </a>
       (present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Sz%C5%91ny" title="Szőny">
        Szőny
       </a>
       at the Slovak-Hungarian border). Such Roman border settlements were built on the present area of Rusovce, currently a suburb of Bratislava. The military fort was surrounded by a civilian vicus and several farms of the villa rustica type. The name of this settlement was
       <a href="/wiki/Gerulata" title="Gerulata">
        Gerulata
       </a>
       . The military fort had an auxiliary cavalry unit, approximately 300 horses strong, modelled after the
       <a href="/wiki/Cananefates" title="Cananefates">
        Cananefates
       </a>
       . The remains of Roman buildings have also survived in Devin castle (present-day downtown Bratislava), the suburbs of Dúbravka and Stupava, and Bratislava Castle Hill.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Trencin-Roman2.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Trencin-Roman2.JPG/220px-Trencin-Roman2.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Trencin-Roman2.JPG/330px-Trencin-Roman2.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Trencin-Roman2.JPG/440px-Trencin-Roman2.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Trencin-Roman2.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A Roman inscription at the castle hill of
         <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="Trenčín">
          Trenčín
         </a>
         (178–179 AD)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Near the northernmost line of the Roman hinterlands, the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Limes_Romanus" title="Limes Romanus">
        Limes Romanus
       </a>
       , there existed the winter camp of
       <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="Trenčín">
        Laugaricio
       </a>
       (modern-day
       <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="Trenčín">
        Trenčín
       </a>
       ) where the Auxiliary of Legion II fought and prevailed in a decisive battle over the Germanic
       <a href="/wiki/Quadi" title="Quadi">
        Quadi
       </a>
       tribe in 179 AD during the
       <a href="/wiki/Marcomannic_Wars" title="Marcomannic Wars">
        Marcomannic Wars
       </a>
       . The Kingdom of
       <a href="/wiki/Vannius" title="Vannius">
        Vannius
       </a>
       , a kingdom founded by the
       <a href="/wiki/Germanic_peoples" title="Germanic peoples">
        Germanic
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">
        Suebian
       </a>
       tribes of
       <a href="/wiki/Quadi" title="Quadi">
        Quadi
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Marcomanni" title="Marcomanni">
        Marcomanni
       </a>
       , as well as several small Germanic and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Celtic_tribes" title="List of Celtic tribes">
        Celtic tribes
       </a>
       , including the Osi and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cotini" title="Cotini">
        Cotini
       </a>
       , existed in Western and Central Slovakia from 8–6 BC to 179 AD.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Great_invasions_from_the_4th_to_7th_centuries">
        Great invasions from the 4th to 7th centuries
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Great invasions from the 4th to 7th centuries">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the 2nd and 3rd centuries AD, the
       <a href="/wiki/Huns" title="Huns">
        Huns
       </a>
       began to leave the Central Asian steppes. They crossed the Danube in 377 AD and occupied
       <a href="/wiki/Pannonia" title="Pannonia">
        Pannonia
       </a>
       , which they used for 75 years as their base for launching looting-raids into Western Europe. However, Attila's death in 453 brought about the disappearance of the Hun tribe. In 568, a Turko-Mongol tribal confederacy, the
       <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Avars" title="Pannonian Avars">
        Avars
       </a>
       , conducted its own invasion into the Middle Danube region. The Avars occupied the lowlands of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pannonian_Plain" title="Pannonian Plain">
        Pannonian Plain
       </a>
       , and established an empire dominating the
       <a href="/wiki/Pannonian_Basin" title="Pannonian Basin">
        Carpathian Basin
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 623, the Slavic population living in the western parts of Pannonia seceded from their empire after a revolution led by Samo, a Frankish merchant.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Történeti_Kronológia_24-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Történeti_Kronológia-24">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After 626, the Avar power started a gradual decline
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but its reign lasted to 804.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Slavic_states">
        Slavic states
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Slavic states">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" title="Slavic peoples">
        Slavic
       </a>
       tribes settled in the territory of present-day Slovakia in the 5th century. Western Slovakia was the centre of
       <a href="/wiki/Samo" title="Samo">
        Samo
       </a>
       's empire in the 7th century. A Slavic state known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Nitra" title="Principality of Nitra">
        Principality of Nitra
       </a>
       arose in the 8th century and its ruler
       <a href="/wiki/Pribina" title="Pribina">
        Pribina
       </a>
       had the first known Christian church of the territory of present-day Slovakia consecrated by 828. Together with neighbouring
       <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">
        Moravia
       </a>
       , the principality formed the core of the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">
        Great Moravian
       </a>
       Empire from 833. The high point of this Slavonic empire came with the arrival of
       <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">
        Saints Cyril and Methodius
       </a>
       in 863, during the reign of
       <a href="/wiki/Duke" title="Duke">
        Duke
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Rastislav_of_Moravia" title="Rastislav of Moravia">
        Rastislav
       </a>
       , and the territorial expansion under
       <a href="/wiki/Duke" title="Duke">
        Duke
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sv%C3%A4topluk_I" title="Svätopluk I">
        Svätopluk I
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Great_Moravia_.28830.E2.80.93before_907.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Great_Moravia_(830–before_907)">
        Great Moravia (830–before 907)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Great Moravia (830–before 907)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">
        Great Moravia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1600" data-file-width="1071" height="224" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg/150px-Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg/225px-Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg/300px-Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cyril_a_metod_zilina.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A statue of
         <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">
          Saint Cyril and Saint Methodius
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDilina" title="Žilina">
          Žilina
         </a>
         . In 863, they introduced Christianity to what is now Slovakia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Great Moravia arose around 830 when
       <a href="/wiki/Mojmir_I_of_Moravia" title="Mojmir I of Moravia">
        Mojmír I
       </a>
       unified the Slavic tribes settled north of the
       <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">
        Danube
       </a>
       and extended the Moravian supremacy over them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       When Mojmír I endeavoured to secede from the supremacy of the king of
       <a href="/wiki/East_Francia" title="East Francia">
        East Francia
       </a>
       in 846, King
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_German" title="Louis the German">
        Louis the German
       </a>
       deposed him and assisted Mojmír's nephew
       <a href="/wiki/Rastislav_of_Moravia" title="Rastislav of Moravia">
        Rastislav
       </a>
       (846–870) in acquiring the throne.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Korai_Magyar_Történeti_Lexikon_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Korai_Magyar_Történeti_Lexikon-27">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The new monarch pursued an independent policy: after stopping a Frankish attack in 855, he also sought to weaken influence of Frankish priests preaching in his realm. Duke Rastislav asked the
       <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">
        Byzantine Emperor
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_III" title="Michael III">
        Michael III
       </a>
       to send teachers who would interpret Christianity in the Slavic vernacular.
      </p>
      <p>
       Upon Rastislav's request, two brothers, Byzantine officials and missionaries
       <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">
        Saints Cyril and Methodius
       </a>
       came in 863. Cyril developed the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glagolitic_alphabet" title="Glagolitic alphabet">
        first Slavic alphabet
       </a>
       and translated the Gospel into the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">
        Old Church Slavonic
       </a>
       language. Rastislav was also preoccupied with the security and administration of his state. Numerous fortified castles built throughout the country are dated to his reign and some of them (e.g.,
       <i>
        Dowina
       </i>
       , sometimes identified with
       <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn_Castle" title="Devín Castle">
        Devín Castle
       </a>
       )
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-worldarcheology_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-worldarcheology-28">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caplovic_29-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-caplovic-29">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       are also mentioned in connection with Rastislav by Frankish chronicles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fulda_31-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-fulda-31">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Letter_svatopluk.jpg">
         <img alt='The papal letter "Industriae Tuae"' class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2016" data-file-width="1624" height="223" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Letter_svatopluk.jpg/180px-Letter_svatopluk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Letter_svatopluk.jpg/270px-Letter_svatopluk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/73/Letter_svatopluk.jpg/360px-Letter_svatopluk.jpg 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Letter_svatopluk.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <i>
          Scire vos volumus
         </i>
         , a letter written in 879 by
         <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_VIII" title="Pope John VIII">
          Pope John VIII
         </a>
         to
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Svatopluk_I" title="Svatopluk I">
          Svatopluk I
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During Rastislav's reign, the
       <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Nitra" title="Principality of Nitra">
        Principality of Nitra
       </a>
       was given to his nephew
       <a href="/wiki/Svatopluk_I_of_Moravia" title="Svatopluk I of Moravia">
        Svätopluk
       </a>
       as an
       <a href="/wiki/Appanage" title="Appanage">
        appanage
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caplovic_29-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-caplovic-29">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The rebellious prince allied himself with the Franks and overthrew his uncle in 870. Similarly to his predecessor, Svätopluk I (871–894) assumed the title of the king (
       <i>
        rex
       </i>
       ). During his reign, the Great Moravian Empire reached its greatest territorial extent, when not only present-day
       <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">
        Moravia
       </a>
       and Slovakia but also present-day northern and
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Hungary" title="Central Hungary">
        central Hungary
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lower_Austria" title="Lower Austria">
        Lower Austria
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">
        Bohemia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Silesia" title="Silesia">
        Silesia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lusatia" title="Lusatia">
        Lusatia
       </a>
       , southern Poland and
       <a class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" href="/wiki/Northern_Serbia" title="Northern Serbia">
        northern Serbia
       </a>
       belonged to the empire, but the exact borders of his domains are still disputed by modern authors.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tóth_32-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Tóth-32">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Svatopluk also withstood attacks of the semi-nomadic
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarians" title="Hungarians">
        Magyar
       </a>
       tribes and the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Bulgarian_Empire" title="First Bulgarian Empire">
        Bulgarian Empire
       </a>
       , although sometimes it was he who hired the Magyars when waging war against East Francia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 880,
       <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_VIII" title="Pope John VIII">
        Pope John VIII
       </a>
       set up an independent
       <a href="/wiki/Ecclesiastical_province" title="Ecclesiastical province">
        ecclesiastical province
       </a>
       in Great Moravia with Archbishop
       <a href="/wiki/Saints_Cyril_and_Methodius" title="Saints Cyril and Methodius">
        Methodius
       </a>
       as its head. He also named the German cleric
       <a href="/wiki/Wiching" title="Wiching">
        Wiching
       </a>
       the Bishop of
       <a href="/wiki/Nitra" title="Nitra">
        Nitra
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       After the death of Prince Svatopluk in 894, his sons
       <a href="/wiki/Mojmir_II_of_Moravia" title="Mojmir II of Moravia">
        Mojmír II
       </a>
       (894–906?) and
       <a href="/wiki/Svatopluk_II" title="Svatopluk II">
        Svatopluk II
       </a>
       succeeded him as the Prince of Great Moravia and the Prince of Nitra respectively.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-caplovic_29-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-caplovic-29">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, they started to quarrel for domination of the whole empire. Weakened by an internal conflict as well as by constant warfare with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eastern_Francia" title="Eastern Francia">
        Eastern Francia
       </a>
       , Great Moravia lost most of its peripheral territories.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Great_Moravia_Svatopluk.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="878" data-file-width="1214" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Great_Moravia_Svatopluk.jpg/220px-Great_Moravia_Svatopluk.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Great_Moravia_Svatopluk.jpg/330px-Great_Moravia_Svatopluk.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Great_Moravia_Svatopluk.jpg/440px-Great_Moravia_Svatopluk.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Great_Moravia_Svatopluk.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Certain and disputed borders of Great Moravia under
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Svatopluk_I" title="Svatopluk I">
          Svatopluk I
         </a>
         (according to modern historians)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In the meantime, the semi-nomadic Magyar tribes, possibly having suffered defeat from the similarly nomadic
       <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">
        Pechenegs
       </a>
       , left their territories east of the
       <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">
        Carpathian Mountains
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       invaded the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carpathian_Basin" title="Carpathian Basin">
        Carpathian Basin
       </a>
       and started to occupy the territory gradually around 896.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Their armies' advance may have been promoted by continuous wars among the countries of the region whose rulers still hired them occasionally to intervene in their struggles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kristó_2_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kristó_2-36">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       It is not known what happened with both Mojmír II and Svatopluk II because they are not mentioned in written sources after 906. In
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Pressburg" title="Battle of Pressburg">
        three battles
       </a>
       (4–5 July and 9 August 907) near
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
        Bratislava
       </a>
       , the Magyars routed
       <a href="/wiki/Bavaria" title="Bavaria">
        Bavarian
       </a>
       armies. Some historians put this year as the date of the break-up of the Great Moravian Empire, due to the Hungarian conquest; other historians take the date a little bit earlier (to 902).
      </p>
      <p>
       Great Moravia left behind a lasting legacy in Central and Eastern Europe. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Glagolitic_alphabet" title="Glagolitic alphabet">
        Glagolitic script
       </a>
       and its successor
       <a href="/wiki/Cyrillic_script" title="Cyrillic script">
        Cyrillic
       </a>
       were disseminated to other Slavic countries, charting a new path in their
       <a href="/wiki/Sociocultural_evolution" title="Sociocultural evolution">
        sociocultural development
       </a>
       . The administrative system of
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">
        Great Moravia
       </a>
       may have influenced the development of the administration of the
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Kingdom_of_Hungary_.281000.E2.80.931918.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kingdom_of_Hungary_(1000–1918)">
        Kingdom of Hungary (1000–1918)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Kingdom of Hungary (1000–1918)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="823" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg/220px-Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg/330px-Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d9/Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg/440px-Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Istvan-ChroniconPictum.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Stephen_I_of_Hungary" title="Stephen I of Hungary">
          Stephen I
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/King_of_Hungary" title="King of Hungary">
          King of Hungary
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Following the disintegration of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Moravian_Empire" title="Great Moravian Empire">
        Great Moravian Empire
       </a>
       at the turn of the 10th century, the Hungarians annexed the territory comprising modern Slovakia. After their defeat on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lech_River" title="Lech River">
        Lech River
       </a>
       they abandoned their nomadic ways; they settled in the centre of the Carpathian valley, adopted Christianity and began to build a new state – the Hungarian kingdom.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From the 11th century, when the territory inhabited by the Slavic-speaking population of Danubian Basin was incorporated into the Kingdom of Hungary, until 1918, when the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_empire" title="Austro-Hungarian empire">
        Austro-Hungarian empire
       </a>
       collapsed, the territory of modern Slovakia was an integral part of the Hungarian state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The ethnic composition became more diverse with the arrival of the
       <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Germans" title="Carpathian Germans">
        Carpathian Germans
       </a>
       in the 13th century, and the
       <a href="/wiki/Jews" title="Jews">
        Jews
       </a>
       in the 14th century.
      </p>
      <p>
       A significant decline in the population resulted from the
       <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">
        invasion of the Mongols
       </a>
       in 1241 and the subsequent famine. However, in medieval times the area of the present-day Slovakia was characterised by German and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jewish" title="Jewish">
        Jewish
       </a>
       immigration, burgeoning towns, construction of numerous stone castles, and the cultivation of the arts.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tibensky_41-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tibensky-41">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1465, King
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Matthias_Corvinus_of_Hungary" title="Matthias Corvinus of Hungary">
        Matthias Corvinus
       </a>
       founded the Hungarian Kingdom's third university, in Pressburg (Bratislava, Pozsony), but it was closed in 1490 after his death.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Hussites" title="Hussites">
        Hussites
       </a>
       also settled in the region after the
       <a href="/wiki/Hussite_Wars" title="Hussite Wars">
        Hussite Wars
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_43-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Central_europe_1683.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1170" data-file-width="1543" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Central_europe_1683.png/220px-Central_europe_1683.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Central_europe_1683.png/330px-Central_europe_1683.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Central_europe_1683.png/440px-Central_europe_1683.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Central_europe_1683.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Royal Hungary, Principality of
         <a href="/wiki/Upper_Hungary" title="Upper Hungary">
          Upper Hungary
         </a>
         , Principality of Transylvania and Ottoman
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Eyalets" title="Eyalets">
          eyalets
         </a>
         around 1683
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Owing to the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman Empire
       </a>
       's expansion into Hungarian territory,
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
        Bratislava
       </a>
       was designated the new capital of Hungary in 1536, ahead of the old Hungarian capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Buda" title="Buda">
        Buda
       </a>
       falling in 1541. It become part of the Austrian Habsburg monarchy, marking the beginning of a new era. The territory comprising modern Slovakia, then known as
       <a href="/wiki/Upper_Hungary" title="Upper Hungary">
        Upper Hungary
       </a>
       , became the place of settlement for nearly two-thirds of the
       <a href="/wiki/Magyar_tribes" title="Magyar tribes">
        Magyar
       </a>
       nobility fleeing the Turks and far more linguistically and culturally Hungarian than it was before.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_43-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Partly thanks to old
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hussite" title="Hussite">
        Hussite
       </a>
       families, and Slovaks studying under
       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">
        Martin Luther
       </a>
       , the region then experienced a growth in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestants" title="Protestants">
        Protestants
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_43-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       For a short period in the 17th century, most Slovaks were Lutherans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_43-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They defied the Catholic Habsburgs and sought protection from neighboring
       <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">
        Transylvania
       </a>
       , a rival continuation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Magyar_tribes" title="Magyar tribes">
        Magyar
       </a>
       state that practiced religious tolerance and normally had Ottoman backing. Upper Hungary, modern Slovakia, became the site of frequent wars between Catholics in the west territory and Protestants in the east, also against Turks, the frontier was on a constant state of military alert and heavily fortified by castles and citadels often manned by Catholic German and Slovak troops on the Habsburg side. In 1655, the printing press at the
       <a href="/wiki/Trnava" title="Trnava">
        Trnava
       </a>
       university produced the Jesuit Benedikt Szöllősi's Cantus Catholici, a Catholic hymnal in the Slovak language that reaffirmed links to the earlier works of Cyril and Methodius. The
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_wars_in_Europe" title="Ottoman wars in Europe">
        Ottoman wars
       </a>
       , rivalry between
       <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">
        Austria
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">
        Transylvania
       </a>
       , and the frequent insurrections against the
       <a href="/wiki/Habsburg_Monarchy" title="Habsburg Monarchy">
        Habsburg Monarchy
       </a>
       inflicted a great deal of devastation, especially in the rural areas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Turkish_War_(1663%E2%80%931664)" title="Austro-Turkish War (1663–1664)">
        Austro-Turkish War (1663–1664)
       </a>
       a Turkish army led by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Vizier" title="Grand Vizier">
        Grand Vizier
       </a>
       decimated Slovakia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-books.google.pl_43-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-books.google.pl-43">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Even so, Slovaks from the
       <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Upper_Hungary" title="Principality of Upper Hungary">
        Principality of Upper Hungary
       </a>
       fought alongside the Turks against the Austrians at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">
        Battle of Vienna
       </a>
       of 1683. As the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Turkish_War" title="Great Turkish War">
        Turks withdrew
       </a>
       from Hungary in the late 17th century, the importance of the territory comprising modern Slovakia decreased, although
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pressburg" title="Pressburg">
        Pressburg
       </a>
       retained its status as the capital of Hungary until 1848, when it was transferred back to Buda.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:1franci2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1334" data-file-width="1062" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/1franci2.jpg/150px-1franci2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/1franci2.jpg/225px-1franci2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/1franci2.jpg/300px-1franci2.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:1franci2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A Slovak volunteers' corp during the
         <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Uprising_of_1848%E2%80%9349" title="Slovak Uprising of 1848–49">
          fight for independence from the Kingdom of Hungary
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848_in_the_Habsburg_areas" title="Revolutions of 1848 in the Habsburg areas">
        revolution of 1848–49
       </a>
       , the Slovaks supported the
       <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Austria" title="Emperor of Austria">
        Austrian Emperor
       </a>
       , hoping for independence from the Hungarian part of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austria%E2%80%93Hungary" title="Austria–Hungary">
        Dual Monarchy
       </a>
       , but they failed to achieve their aim. Thereafter relations between the nationalities deteriorated (see
       <a href="/wiki/Magyarization" title="Magyarization">
        Magyarization
       </a>
       ), culminating in the secession of Slovakia from Hungary after World War I.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Czechoslovakia_.281918.E2.80.931939.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Czechoslovakia_(1918–1939)">
        Czechoslovakia (1918–1939)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Czechoslovakia (1918–1939)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">
        Czechoslovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2136" data-file-width="2848" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg/220px-Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg/330px-Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a5/Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg/440px-Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Masaryk_a_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A monument to
         <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Garrigue_Masaryk" title="Tomáš Garrigue Masaryk">
          Tomáš Garrigue Masaryk
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Milan_Rastislav_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik" title="Milan Rastislav Štefánik">
          Milan Štefánik
         </a>
         – both key figures in early Czechoslovakia
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 1918, Slovakia and the regions of
       <a href="/wiki/Bohemia" title="Bohemia">
        Bohemia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Moravia" title="Moravia">
        Moravia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Silesia" title="Czech Silesia">
        Czech Silesia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Ruthenia" title="Carpathian Ruthenia">
        Carpathian Ruthenia
       </a>
       formed a common state,
       <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">
        Czechoslovakia
       </a>
       , with the borders confirmed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Saint-Germain-en-Laye_(1919)" title="Treaty of Saint-Germain-en-Laye (1919)">
        Treaty of Saint Germain
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Trianon" title="Treaty of Trianon">
        Treaty of Trianon
       </a>
       . In 1919, during the chaos following the break-up of Austria-Hungary, Czechoslovakia was formed with numerous Germans and Hungarians within the newly set borders. A Slovak patriot
       <a href="/wiki/Milan_Rastislav_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik" title="Milan Rastislav Štefánik">
        Milan Rastislav Štefánik
       </a>
       (1880–1919), who helped organise Czechoslovak regiments against Austria-Hungary during the First World War, died in a plane crash. In the peace following the World War, Czechoslovakia emerged as a sovereign European state. It provided what were at the time rather extensive rights to its minorities and remained the only democracy in this part of Europe in the interwar period.
      </p>
      <p>
       During the
       <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">
        Interwar period
       </a>
       , democratic Czechoslovakia was allied with France, and also with
       <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
        Romania
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Yugoslavia" title="Yugoslavia">
        Yugoslavia
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Little_Entente" title="Little Entente">
        Little Entente
       </a>
       ); however, the
       <a href="/wiki/Locarno_Treaties" title="Locarno Treaties">
        Locarno Treaties
       </a>
       of 1925 left East European security open. Both Czechs and Slovaks enjoyed a period of relative prosperity. There was progress in not only the development of the country's economy, but also culture and educational opportunities. The minority Germans came to accept their role in the new country and relations with Austria were good. Yet the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">
        Great Depression
       </a>
       caused a sharp economic downturn, followed by political disruption and insecurity in Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Thereafter Czechoslovakia came under continuous pressure from the
       <a href="/wiki/Revanchism" title="Revanchism">
        revisionist
       </a>
       governments of Germany and Hungary. Eventually this led to the
       <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">
        Munich Agreement
       </a>
       of September 1938, which allowed Nazi Germany to partially dismember the country by occupying what was called the
       <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">
        Sudetenland
       </a>
       , a region with a German-speaking majority and bordering Germany and Austria. The remainder of "rump" Czechoslovakia was renamed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Czecho-Slovakia" title="Czecho-Slovakia">
        Czecho-Slovakia
       </a>
       and included a greater degree of Slovak political autonomy. Southern and eastern Slovakia, however, was reclaimed by Hungary at the
       <a href="/wiki/First_Vienna_Award" title="First Vienna Award">
        First Vienna Award
       </a>
       of November 1938.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="World_War_II_.281939.E2.80.931945.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="World_War_II_(1939–1945)">
        World War II (1939–1945)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: World War II (1939–1945)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Slovak Republic (1939–1945)">
        Slovak Republic (1939–1945)
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Jozef_Tiso_(Berlin).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2436" data-file-width="3500" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Jozef_Tiso_%28Berlin%29.jpg/220px-Jozef_Tiso_%28Berlin%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Jozef_Tiso_%28Berlin%29.jpg/330px-Jozef_Tiso_%28Berlin%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Jozef_Tiso_%28Berlin%29.jpg/440px-Jozef_Tiso_%28Berlin%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Jozef_Tiso_(Berlin).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">
          Adolf Hitler
         </a>
         greeting
         <a href="/wiki/Jozef_Tiso" title="Jozef Tiso">
          Jozef Tiso
         </a>
         , 1941
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After the
       <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">
        Munich Agreement
       </a>
       and its
       <a href="/wiki/Vienna_Award" title="Vienna Award">
        Vienna Award
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       threatened to annex part of Slovakia and allow the remaining regions to be partitioned by Hungary or Poland unless independence was declared. Thus, Slovakia seceded from Czecho-Slovakia in March 1939 and allied itself, as demanded by Germany, with
       <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">
        Hitler's
       </a>
       coalition.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Secession had created the first Slovak state in history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RadioPrague_49-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-RadioPrague-49">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The government of the
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Slovak Republic (1939–1945)">
        First Slovak Republic
       </a>
       , led by
       <a href="/wiki/Jozef_Tiso" title="Jozef Tiso">
        Jozef Tiso
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Vojtech_Tuka" title="Vojtech Tuka">
        Vojtech Tuka
       </a>
       , was strongly influenced by Germany and gradually became a
       <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">
        puppet regime
       </a>
       in many respects.
      </p>
      <p>
       Meanwhile, the
       <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovak_government-in-exile" title="Czechoslovak government-in-exile">
        Czechoslovak government-in-exile
       </a>
       , sought to reverse the
       <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">
        Munich Agreement
       </a>
       and the subsequent German occupation of Czechoslovakia, and to return the Republic to its 1937 boundaries. The government operated from
       <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">
        London
       </a>
       and it was ultimately considered, by those countries that recognised it, the legitimate government for Czechoslovakia throughout the Second World War.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1413" data-file-width="2033" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg/220px-Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg/330px-Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg/440px-Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Nastupeni_povstalci.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Troops of Slovak anti-Nazi
         <a href="/wiki/Resistance_movement" title="Resistance movement">
          resistance movement
         </a>
         in 1944
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       75,000 Jews out of 80,000 who remained on Slovak territory after Hungary had seized southern regions were deported and taken to German
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Death_camps" title="Death camps">
        death camps
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Thousands of Jews, Gypsies and other politically undesirable people remained in Slovak forced labor camps in
       <a href="/wiki/Sere%C4%8F_concentration_camp" title="Sereď concentration camp">
        Sereď
       </a>
       , Vyhne, and Nováky.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Tiso, through the granting of presidential exceptions, allowed between 1,000 and 4,000 people crucial to the war economy to avoid deportations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Under Tiso's government and Hungarian occupation, the vast majority of Slovakia's pre-war Jewish population (between 75,000–105,000 individuals including those who perished from the occupied territory) were murdered.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Slovak state paid Germany 500
       <a href="/wiki/Reichsmark" title="Reichsmark">
        RM
       </a>
       per every deported Jew for "retraining and accommodation" (similar payment, but only 30 RM was paid by
       <a href="/wiki/Independent_State_of_Croatia" title="Independent State of Croatia">
        Croatia
       </a>
       ).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56">
        <a href="#cite_note-56">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       After it became clear that the Soviet
       <a href="/wiki/Red_Army" title="Red Army">
        Red Army
       </a>
       was going to push the Nazis out of eastern and central Europe, an anti-Nazi
       <a href="/wiki/Resistance_movement" title="Resistance movement">
        resistance movement
       </a>
       launched a fierce armed insurrection, known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_National_Uprising" title="Slovak National Uprising">
        Slovak National Uprising
       </a>
       , near the end of summer 1944. A bloody German occupation and a guerilla war followed. Germans and their
       <a href="/wiki/Hlinka_Guard" title="Hlinka Guard">
        local collaborators
       </a>
       completely destroyed 93 villages and massacred thousands of civilians, often hundreds at a time.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57">
        <a href="#cite_note-57">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The territory of Slovakia was liberated by Soviet and Romanian forces by the end of April 1945.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Soviet_influence_and_Communist_party_rule_.281948.E2.80.931989.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Soviet_influence_and_Communist_party_rule_(1948–1989)">
        Soviet influence and Communist party rule (1948–1989)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Soviet influence and Communist party rule (1948–1989)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Alekseev_alexander_4.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="862" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Alekseev_alexander_4.jpg/220px-Alekseev_alexander_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Alekseev_alexander_4.jpg/330px-Alekseev_alexander_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0d/Alekseev_alexander_4.jpg/440px-Alekseev_alexander_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Alekseev_alexander_4.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">
          Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia
         </a>
         in 1968
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="649" data-file-width="1000" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg/220px-Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg/330px-Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg/440px-Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Praha_19891122-419-02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">
          Velvet Revolution
         </a>
         ended 41 years of authoritarian Communist rule in
         <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">
          Czechoslovakia
         </a>
         in 1989.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After World War II, Czechoslovakia was reconstituted and
       <a href="/wiki/Jozef_Tiso" title="Jozef Tiso">
        Jozef Tiso
       </a>
       was executed in 1947 for collaboration with the Nazis. More than
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Slovakia#Population_exchanges" title="Hungarians in Slovakia">
        80,000 Hungarians
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and 32,000 Germans
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       were forced to leave Slovakia, in a series of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_Germans_after_World_War_II" title="Expulsion of Germans after World War II">
        population transfers
       </a>
       initiated by the Allies at the
       <a href="/wiki/Potsdam_Conference" title="Potsdam Conference">
        Potsdam Conference
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rock_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rock-60">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Out of about 130,000
       <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Germans" title="Carpathian Germans">
        Carpathian Germans
       </a>
       in Slovakia in 1938, by 1947 only some 20,000 remained.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As a result of the
       <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">
        Yalta Conference
       </a>
       , Czechoslovakia came under the influence and later under direct occupation of the Soviet Union and its
       <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">
        Warsaw Pact
       </a>
       , after a coup in 1948. The country was
       <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact_invasion_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Warsaw Pact invasion of Czechoslovakia">
        invaded
       </a>
       by the Warsaw Pact forces (with the exception of
       <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">
        Romania
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Albania" title="Albania">
        Albania
       </a>
       ) in 1968, ending a
       <a href="/wiki/Prague_Spring" title="Prague Spring">
        period of liberalisation
       </a>
       under the leadership of
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Dub%C4%8Dek" title="Alexander Dubček">
        Alexander Dubček
       </a>
       . In 1969 Czechoslovakia became a federation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Socialist_Republic" title="Czech Socialist Republic">
        Czech Socialist Republic
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Socialist_Republic" title="Slovak Socialist Republic">
        Slovak Socialist Republic
       </a>
       . Czechoslovakia was never part of the Soviet Union and remained independent to a degree.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Establishment_of_the_Slovak_Republic_.28after_1993.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Establishment_of_the_Slovak_Republic_(after_1993)">
        Establishment of the Slovak Republic (after 1993)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Establishment of the Slovak Republic (after 1993)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The end of Communist rule in Czechoslovakia in 1989, during the peaceful
       <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">
        Velvet Revolution
       </a>
       , was followed once again by the country's dissolution, this time into two
       <a href="/wiki/Succession_of_states" title="Succession of states">
        successor states
       </a>
       . The word "socialist" was dropped in the names of the two republics, i.e. the Slovak Socialist Republic was renamed Slovak Republic. In July 17, 1992 Slovakia, led by Prime Minister
       <a href="/wiki/Vladim%C3%ADr_Me%C4%8Diar" title="Vladimír Mečiar">
        Vladimír Mečiar
       </a>
       , declared itself a sovereign state, meaning that its laws took precedence over those of the federal government. Throughout the autumn of 1992, Mečiar and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Prime_Ministers_of_the_Czech_Republic" title="List of Prime Ministers of the Czech Republic">
        Czech Prime Minister
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/V%C3%A1clav_Klaus" title="Václav Klaus">
        Václav Klaus
       </a>
       negotiated the details for disbanding the federation. In November the federal parliament voted to dissolve the country officially on December 31, 1992.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="310" data-file-width="521" height="131" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/220px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/330px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg/440px-Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_%28081%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Tratado_de_Lisboa_13_12_2007_(081).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Slovakia became a member of the European Union in 2004 and signed the
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lisbon_Treaty" title="Lisbon Treaty">
          Lisbon Treaty
         </a>
         in 2007.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Slovak Republic and the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
        Czech Republic
       </a>
       went their separate ways after 1 January 1993, an event sometimes called the
       <a href="/wiki/Dissolution_of_Czechoslovakia" title="Dissolution of Czechoslovakia">
        Velvet Divorce
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Slovakia has remained a close partner with the Czech Republic. Both countries co-operate with Hungary and Poland in the
       <a href="/wiki/Visegr%C3%A1d_Group" title="Visegrád Group">
        Visegrád Group
       </a>
       . Slovakia became a member of NATO on 29 March 2004 and of the European Union on 1 May 2004. On 1 January 2009, Slovakia adopted the
       <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">
        Euro
       </a>
       as its national currency.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Slovakia" title="Geography of Slovakia">
        Geography of Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Geomorphological_division_of_Slovakia" title="Geomorphological division of Slovakia">
        Geomorphological division of Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Slovakia lies between latitudes
       <a href="/wiki/47th_parallel_north" title="47th parallel north">
        47°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/50th_parallel_north" title="50th parallel north">
        50° N
       </a>
       , and longitudes
       <a href="/wiki/16th_meridian_east" title="16th meridian east">
        16°
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/23rd_meridian_east" title="23rd meridian east">
        23° E
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The Slovak landscape is noted primarily for its mountainous nature, with the
       <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">
        Carpathian Mountains
       </a>
       extending across most of the northern half of the country. Amongst these
       <a href="/wiki/Mountain_range" title="Mountain range">
        mountain ranges
       </a>
       are the high peaks of the
       <a href="/wiki/Fatra-Tatra_Area" title="Fatra-Tatra Area">
        Fatra-Tatra Area
       </a>
       (including
       <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">
        Tatra Mountains
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ve%C4%BEk%C3%A1_Fatra" title="Veľká Fatra">
        Greater Fatra
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lesser_Fatra" title="Lesser Fatra">
        Lesser Fatra
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Ore_Mountains" title="Slovak Ore Mountains">
        Slovak Ore Mountains
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Central_Mountains" title="Slovak Central Mountains">
        Slovak Central Mountains
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Beskids" title="Beskids">
        Beskids
       </a>
       . The largest lowland is the fertile
       <a href="/wiki/Danubian_Lowland" title="Danubian Lowland">
        Danubian Lowland
       </a>
       in the southwest, followed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Slovak_Lowland" title="Eastern Slovak Lowland">
        Eastern Slovak Lowland
       </a>
       in the southeast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-64">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Forests cover 41% of Slovak land surface.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Tatra_mountains">
        Tatra mountains
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Tatra mountains">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Mountains" title="Tatra Mountains">
        Tatra Mountains
       </a>
      </div>

         </a>
        </div>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:High_Tatras_Panorama.jpg" title="File:High Tatras Panorama.jpg">
          </a>
         </div>
         Panorama of the
         <a href="/wiki/High_Tatras" title="High Tatras">
          High Tatras
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">

           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="gallerytext">
          <p>
           <a href="/wiki/Gerlachovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt" title="Gerlachovský štít">
            Gerlachovský štít
           </a>
           (2,655 metres or 8,711 feet), the highest peak in Slovakia
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 162px">
        <div style="width: 162px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 160px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kriv%C3%A1%C5%88.JPG">

           </a>
          </div>
         </div>

           <a href="/wiki/Kriv%C3%A1%C5%88_(peak)" title="Kriváň (peak)">
            Kriváň
           </a>
           (2,495 metres or 8,186 feet), the country's symbol on 1,2 and 5 euro cents
          </p>
         </div>
        </div>
       </li>
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 182px">
        <div style="width: 182px">
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 180px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">
           <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:STANICA_LANOVKY_S_OBSERVAT%C3%93RIOM_-_v%C3%BDhlad.JPG">

           </a>
          </div>
         </div>
