      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Slovakia" title="Economy of Slovakia">
        Economy of Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:National_Bank_of_Slovakia,_Bratislava.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4958" data-file-width="3305" height="255" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/National_Bank_of_Slovakia%2C_Bratislava.jpg/170px-National_Bank_of_Slovakia%2C_Bratislava.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/National_Bank_of_Slovakia%2C_Bratislava.jpg/255px-National_Bank_of_Slovakia%2C_Bratislava.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/National_Bank_of_Slovakia%2C_Bratislava.jpg/340px-National_Bank_of_Slovakia%2C_Bratislava.jpg 2x" width="170"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:National_Bank_of_Slovakia,_Bratislava.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/National_Bank_of_Slovakia" title="National Bank of Slovakia">
          National Bank of Slovakia
         </a>
         in Bratislava
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Slovak economy is a developed,
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_high-income_economy" title="World Bank high-income economy">
        high-income
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83">
        <a href="#cite_note-83">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       economy, with the GDP per capita equalling 77% of the average of the European Union in 2016.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rich_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rich-84">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The country has difficulties addressing regional imbalances in wealth and employment.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85">
        <a href="#cite_note-85">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       GDP per capita ranges from 188% of EU average in Bratislava to 54% in Eastern Slovakia.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/OECD" title="OECD">
        OECD
       </a>
       in 2017 reported:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        "The Slovak Republic continues exhibiting robust economic performance, with strong growth backed by a sound financial sector, low public debt and high international competitiveness drawing on large inward investment."
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86">
         <a href="#cite_note-86">
          [85]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       In 2016, Slovakia was ranked as the 40th
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GDP_(nominal)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GDP (nominal) per capita">
        richest country in the world
       </a>
       , with a nominal per capita GDP of $16,499. The country used to be dubbed the "
       <a href="/wiki/Tatra_Tiger" title="Tatra Tiger">
        Tatra Tiger
       </a>
       ". Slovakia successfully transformed from a centrally
       <a href="/wiki/Planned_economy" title="Planned economy">
        planned economy
       </a>
       to a market-driven economy. Major
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privatisation" title="Privatisation">
        privatisations
       </a>
       are completed, the banking sector is almost completely in private hands, and foreign investment has risen.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:162px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eurozone.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="456" data-file-width="450" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/160px-Eurozone.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/240px-Eurozone.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/08/Eurozone.svg/320px-Eurozone.svg.png 2x" width="160"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eurozone.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Slovakia is part of the
         <a href="/wiki/Schengen_Area" title="Schengen Area">
          Schengen Area
         </a>
         , the EU single market, and since 2009, the
         <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">
          Eurozone
         </a>
         (dark blue)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Slovak economy is one of the fastest growing economies in Europe and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_real_GDP_growth_rate" title="List of countries by real GDP growth rate">
        3rd fastest
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Eurozone" title="Eurozone">
        eurozone
       </a>
       (2017). In 2007, 2008 and 2010 (with
       <a href="/wiki/Gross_domestic_product" title="Gross domestic product">
        GDP
       </a>
       growth of 10.5%, 6% and 4% retrospectively). In 2016, more than 86% of Slovak exports went to
       <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">
        European Union
       </a>
       , and more than 50% of Slovak imports came from other European Union member states.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87">
        <a href="#cite_note-87">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The ratio of government debt to GDP in Slovakia reached 52% by the end of 2016, far below the OECD average.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88">
        <a href="#cite_note-88">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Unemployment, peaking at 19% at the end of 1999, decreased to 5,95% at the end of 2017, lowest recorded rate in Slovak history.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89">
        <a href="#cite_note-89">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Inflation dropped from an average annual rate of 12% in 2000 to just 3.3% in 2002, an election year, but it rose again in 2003–2004 because of rising labour costs and taxes. It reached only 1% in 2010 which is the lowest recorded rate since 1993.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The rate was at 4% in 2011.
      </p>
      <p>
       Slovakia adopted the Euro currency on 1 January 2009 as the 16th member of the Eurozone. The euro in Slovakia was approved by
       <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">
        the European commission
       </a>
       on 7 May 2008. The
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_koruna" title="Slovak koruna">
        Slovak koruna
       </a>
       was revalued on 28 May 2008 to 30.126 for 1 euro,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which was also the exchange rate for the euro.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg/220px-Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg/330px-Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/40/Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg/440px-Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bratislava_highrises_2009_4.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         High-rise buildings in Bratislava's business districts
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Slovakia is an attractive country for
       <a href="/wiki/Investment" title="Investment">
        foreign investors
       </a>
       mainly because of its low wages, low tax rates and well educated
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Labor_force" title="Labor force">
        labour force
       </a>
       . In recent years, Slovakia has been pursuing a policy of encouraging foreign investment.
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_direct_investment" title="Foreign direct investment">
        FDI
       </a>
       inflow grew more than 600% from 2000 and cumulatively reached an all-time high of $17.3 billion in 2006, or around $22,000 per capita by the end of 2008.
      </p>
      <p>
       In March 2008, the Ministry of Finance announced that Slovakia's economy is developed enough to stop being an aid receiver from the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Bank" title="World Bank">
        World Bank
       </a>
       . Slovakia became an aid provider at the end of 2008.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Industry">
        Industry
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Industry">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Slovakia" title="Automotive industry in Slovakia">
        Automotive industry in Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg/220px-Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg/330px-Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg/440px-Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Aupark_Tower_2009.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/ESET" title="ESET">
          ESET
         </a>
         headquarters in Bratislava
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Although Slovakia's GDP comes mainly from the tertiary (services) sector, the industrial sector also plays an important role within its economy. The main industry sectors are
       <a href="/wiki/Automotive_industry_in_Slovakia" title="Automotive industry in Slovakia">
        car manufacturing
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Electrical_engineering" title="Electrical engineering">
        electrical engineering
       </a>
       . Since 2007, Slovakia has been the world's largest producer of cars per capita,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kia_94-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kia-94">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       with a total of 1.040.000 cars manufactured in the country in 2016 alone.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-touchit.sk_20-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-touchit.sk-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There are currently three automobile assembly plants:
       <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">
        Volkswagen
       </a>
       's in
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
        Bratislava
       </a>
       (models:
       <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Up" title="Volkswagen Up">
        Volkswagen Up
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Touareg" title="Volkswagen Touareg">
        Volkswagen Touareg
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Audi_Q7" title="Audi Q7">
        Audi Q7
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Porsche_Cayenne" title="Porsche Cayenne">
        Porsche Cayenne
       </a>
       ),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/PSA_Peugeot_Citro%C3%ABn" title="PSA Peugeot Citroën">
        PSA Peugeot Citroën
       </a>
       's in
       <a href="/wiki/Trnava" title="Trnava">
        Trnava
       </a>
       (models:
       <a href="/wiki/Peugeot_208" title="Peugeot 208">
        Peugeot 208
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Citro%C3%ABn_C3_Picasso" title="Citroën C3 Picasso">
        Citroën C3 Picasso
       </a>
       ) and
       <a href="/wiki/Kia_Motors" title="Kia Motors">
        Kia Motors
       </a>
       '
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kia_Design_and_Manufacturing_Facilities#Žilina_Plant" title="Kia Design and Manufacturing Facilities">
        Žilina Plant
       </a>
       (models:
       <a href="/wiki/Kia_Cee%27d" title="Kia Cee'd">
        Kia Cee'd
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kia_Sportage" title="Kia Sportage">
        Kia Sportage
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kia_Venga" title="Kia Venga">
        Kia Venga
       </a>
       ). In 2018,
       <a href="/wiki/Jaguar_Land_Rover" title="Jaguar Land Rover">
        Jaguar Land Rover
       </a>
       is set to open the country's fourth automobile assembly plant in
       <a href="/wiki/Nitra" title="Nitra">
        Nitra
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From electrical engineering companies,
       <a href="/wiki/Foxconn" title="Foxconn">
        Foxconn
       </a>
       has a factory at
       <a href="/wiki/Nitra" title="Nitra">
        Nitra
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/LCD_television" title="LCD television">
        LCD TV
       </a>
       manufacturing,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Samsung_Group" title="Samsung Group">
        Samsung
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Galanta" title="Galanta">
        Galanta
       </a>
       for
       <a href="/wiki/Computer_monitor" title="Computer monitor">
        computer monitors
       </a>
       and television sets manufacturing.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/ESET" title="ESET">
        ESET
       </a>
       is an IT security company from Bratislava with more than 1,000
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       employees worldwide at present. Their branch offices are in the United States,
       <a href="/wiki/Ireland" title="Ireland">
        Ireland
       </a>
       , United Kingdom,
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
        Czech Republic
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">
        Singapore
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">
        Poland
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_Export_Treemap.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="747" data-file-width="964" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Slovakia_Export_Treemap.png/220px-Slovakia_Export_Treemap.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Slovakia_Export_Treemap.png/330px-Slovakia_Export_Treemap.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/96/Slovakia_Export_Treemap.png/440px-Slovakia_Export_Treemap.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_Export_Treemap.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A graphical depiction of Slovakia's product exports in 28 colour-coded categories
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Bratislava's geographical position in Central Europe has long made Bratislava a crossroads for
       <a href="/wiki/International_trade" title="International trade">
        international trade
       </a>
       traffic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98">
        <a href="#cite_note-98">
         [97]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99">
        <a href="#cite_note-99">
         [98]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Various ancient
       <a href="/wiki/Trade_route" title="Trade route">
        trade routes
       </a>
       , such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Amber_Road" title="Amber Road">
        Amber Road
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">
        Danube
       </a>
       waterway, have crossed territory of present-day Bratislava. Today, Bratislava is the road, railway, waterway and airway hub.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transport_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-transport-100">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">
        Energy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Energy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG/220px-Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG/330px-Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG/440px-Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mochovce_-_chladice_ve%C5%BEe.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Nuclear Power Plant
         <a href="/wiki/Mochovce_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Mochovce Nuclear Power Plant">
          Mochovce
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       In 2012, Slovakia produced a total of 28 393
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/GWh" title="GWh">
        GWh
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Electricity" title="Electricity">
        electricity
       </a>
       while at the same time consumed 28 786 GWh. The slightly higher level of consumption than the capacity of production (- 393 GWh) meant the country was not self-sufficient in energy sourcing. Slovakia imported electricity mainly from the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
        Czech Republic
       </a>
       (9 961 GWh – 73.6% of total import) and exported mainly to
       <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">
        Hungary
       </a>
       (10 231 GWh – 78.2% of total export).
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_power" title="Nuclear power">
        Nuclear energy
       </a>
       accounts for 53.8% of total electricity production in Slovakia, followed by 18.1% of
       <a href="/wiki/Thermal_power_station" title="Thermal power station">
        thermal power
       </a>
       energy, 15.1% by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hydro_power" title="Hydro power">
        hydro power
       </a>
       energy, 2% by
       <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">
        solar energy
       </a>
       , 9.6% by other sources and the rest 1.4% is imported.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         [100]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The two nuclear power-plants in Slovakia are in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaslovsk%C3%A9_Bohunice_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Jaslovské Bohunice Nuclear Power Plant">
        Jaslovské Bohunice
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mochovce_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Mochovce Nuclear Power Plant">
        Mochovce
       </a>
       , each of them containing two operating reactors. Prior to the accession of Slovakia to the EU in 2004, the government agreed to turn-off the V1 block of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaslovsk%C3%A9_Bohunice_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Jaslovské Bohunice Nuclear Power Plant">
        Jaslovské Bohunice power-plant
       </a>
       , built in 1978. After deactivating the last of the two reactors of the V1 block in 2008, Slovakia instantly stopped being self-dependent in energy production. Currently there is another block (V2) with two active reactors in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jaslovsk%C3%A9_Bohunice_Nuclear_Power_Plant" title="Jaslovské Bohunice Nuclear Power Plant">
        Jaslovské Bohunice
       </a>
       . It is scheduled for decommissioning in 2025. Two new reactors are under construction in Mochovce plant. The nuclear power production in Slovakia sometimes draws attention to
       <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">
        Austrian
       </a>
       green-energy activists who occasionally organise protests and block the borders between the two countries.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">
        Transportation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Transportation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Slovakia" title="Transport in Slovakia">
        Transport in Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tnone center">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:632px;max-width:632px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry,_Star%C3%BD_Smokovec,_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD,_jednotka_425.965.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="1941" data-file-width="2588" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Star%C3%BD_Smokovec%2C_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD%2C_jednotka_425.965.jpg/190px-Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Star%C3%BD_Smokovec%2C_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD%2C_jednotka_425.965.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Star%C3%BD_Smokovec%2C_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD%2C_jednotka_425.965.jpg/285px-Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Star%C3%BD_Smokovec%2C_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD%2C_jednotka_425.965.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Star%C3%BD_Smokovec%2C_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD%2C_jednotka_425.965.jpg/380px-Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry%2C_Star%C3%BD_Smokovec%2C_n%C3%A1dra%C5%BE%C3%AD%2C_jednotka_425.965.jpg 2x" width="190"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          A tram in the northern town of
          <a href="/wiki/Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry" title="Vysoké Tatry">
           Vysoké Tatry
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:212px;max-width:212px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:VysokeTatry11Slovakia17.JPG">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="1163" data-file-width="1711" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/VysokeTatry11Slovakia17.JPG/210px-VysokeTatry11Slovakia17.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/VysokeTatry11Slovakia17.JPG/315px-VysokeTatry11Slovakia17.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/15/VysokeTatry11Slovakia17.JPG/420px-VysokeTatry11Slovakia17.JPG 2x" width="210"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorway_D1_(Slovakia)" title="Motorway D1 (Slovakia)">
           D1 motorway
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:222px;max-width:222px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bratislava_-_Milan_Rastislav_Stefanik_(Ivanka)_(BTS_-_LZIB)_AN1902830.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="680" data-file-width="1024" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bratislava_-_Milan_Rastislav_Stefanik_%28Ivanka%29_%28BTS_-_LZIB%29_AN1902830.jpg/220px-Bratislava_-_Milan_Rastislav_Stefanik_%28Ivanka%29_%28BTS_-_LZIB%29_AN1902830.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bratislava_-_Milan_Rastislav_Stefanik_%28Ivanka%29_%28BTS_-_LZIB%29_AN1902830.jpg/330px-Bratislava_-_Milan_Rastislav_Stefanik_%28Ivanka%29_%28BTS_-_LZIB%29_AN1902830.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Bratislava_-_Milan_Rastislav_Stefanik_%28Ivanka%29_%28BTS_-_LZIB%29_AN1902830.jpg/440px-Bratislava_-_Milan_Rastislav_Stefanik_%28Ivanka%29_%28BTS_-_LZIB%29_AN1902830.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <a href="/wiki/Bratislava_Airport" title="Bratislava Airport">
           Bratislava Airport
          </a>
          , the main international airport of Slovakia.
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Highways_in_Slovakia.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="475" data-file-width="842" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Highways_in_Slovakia.svg/220px-Highways_in_Slovakia.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Highways_in_Slovakia.svg/330px-Highways_in_Slovakia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Highways_in_Slovakia.svg/440px-Highways_in_Slovakia.svg.png 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Highways_in_Slovakia.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Highway network in Slovakia as of 2016
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       There are four main highways D1 to D4 and eight express ways R1 to R8. Most of them are still in the planning phase.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorway_D1_(Slovakia)" title="Motorway D1 (Slovakia)">
        D1 motorway
       </a>
       connects Bratislava to
       <a href="/wiki/Trnava" title="Trnava">
        Trnava
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nitra" title="Nitra">
        Nitra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="Trenčín">
        Trenčín
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDilina" title="Žilina">
        Žilina
       </a>
       and beyond, while the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorway_D2_(Slovakia)" title="Motorway D2 (Slovakia)">
        D2 motorway
       </a>
       connects it to
       <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">
        Prague
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Brno" title="Brno">
        Brno
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">
        Budapest
       </a>
       in the north-south direction. A large part of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motorway_D4_(Slovakia)" title="Motorway D4 (Slovakia)">
        D4 motorway
       </a>
       (an outer bypass), which should ease the pressure on Bratislava's highway system, is scheduled to open in 2020.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         [101]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nordostautobahn" title="Nordostautobahn">
        A6 motorway
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">
        Vienna
       </a>
       connects Slovakia directly to the Austrian motorway system and was opened on 19 November 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         [102]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In Bratislava there are currently five bridges standing over the
       <a href="/wiki/Danube" title="Danube">
        Danube
       </a>
       (from upstream to downstream):
       <a href="/wiki/Lafranconi_Bridge" title="Lafranconi Bridge">
        Lafranconi Bridge
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nov%C3%BD_Most" title="Nový Most">
        Nový Most
       </a>
       (The New Bridge or Most SNP),
       <a href="/wiki/Star%C3%BD_most_(Bratislava)" title="Starý most (Bratislava)">
        Starý most
       </a>
       (The Old Bridge),
       <a href="/wiki/Apollo_Bridge" title="Apollo Bridge">
        Most Apollo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Pr%C3%ADstavn%C3%BD_most" title="Prístavný most">
        Prístavný most
       </a>
       (The Harbor Bridge).
      </p>
      <p>
       The city's inner network of roadways is made on the radial-circular shape. Nowadays, the city experiences a sharp increase in the road traffic, increasing pressure on the road network. There are about 200,000 registered cars in Bratislava, (approximately 2 inhabitants per car).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-transport_100-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-transport-100">
         [99]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EJ_671.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="2784" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/EJ_671.JPG/220px-EJ_671.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/EJ_671.JPG/330px-EJ_671.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/EJ_671.JPG/440px-EJ_671.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EJ_671.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         A train of
         <a href="/wiki/Railways_of_Slovak_Republic" title="Railways of Slovak Republic">
          Railways of Slovak Republic
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Bratislava's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M._R._%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik_Airport" title="M. R. Štefánik Airport">
        M. R. Štefánik Airport
       </a>
       is the main
       <a href="/wiki/International_airport" title="International airport">
        international airport
       </a>
       in Slovakia. It is located 9 kilometres (5.6
       <a href="/wiki/Mile" title="Mile">
        miles
       </a>
       ) northeast of the city centre. It serves civil and governmental, scheduled and unscheduled domestic and international flights. The current runways support the landing of all common types of aircraft currently used. The airport has enjoyed rapidly growing passenger traffic in recent years; it served 279,028 passengers in 2000, 1,937,642 in 2006 and 2,024,142 in 2007.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         [103]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Smaller airports served by passenger airlines include those in
       <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="Košice">
        Košice
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Poprad" title="Poprad">
        Poprad
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Bratislava" title="Port of Bratislava">
        Port of Bratislava
       </a>
       is one of the two international
       <a href="/wiki/Port" title="Port">
        river ports
       </a>
       in Slovakia. The port connects Bratislava to international boat traffic, especially the interconnection from the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Sea" title="North Sea">
        North Sea
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Black_Sea" title="Black Sea">
        Black Sea
       </a>
       via the
       <a href="/wiki/Rhine%E2%80%93Main%E2%80%93Danube_Canal" title="Rhine–Main–Danube Canal">
        Rhine-Main-Danube Canal
       </a>
       . Additionally, tourist boats operate from Bratislava's passenger port, including routes to
       <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn" title="Devín">
        Devín
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vienna" title="Vienna">
        Vienna
       </a>
       and elsewhere.
      </p>

        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>

        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px">

          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <a href="/wiki/Old_Town,_Bratislava" title="Old Town, Bratislava">
           The Old Town
          </a>
          in
          <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
           Bratislava
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Slovakia features natural landscapes, mountains,
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_caves_in_Slovakia" title="List of caves in Slovakia">
        caves
       </a>
       , medieval
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_castles_in_Slovakia" title="List of castles in Slovakia">
        castles
       </a>
       and towns, folk architecture, spas and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ski_and_winter_sports_in_Slovakia" title="Ski and winter sports in Slovakia">
        ski resorts
       </a>
       . More than 5 million tourists visited Slovakia in 2016, and the most attractive destinations are the capital of
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
        Bratislava
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/High_Tatras" title="High Tatras">
        High Tatras
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         [104]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most visitors come from the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
        Czech Republic
       </a>
       (about 26%), Poland (15%) and Germany (11%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106">
        <a href="#cite_note-106">
         [105]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Slovakia contains many castles, most of which are in ruins. The best known castles include
       <a href="/wiki/Bojnice_Castle" title="Bojnice Castle">
        Bojnice Castle
       </a>
       (often used as a filming location),
       <a href="/wiki/Spi%C5%A1_Castle" title="Spiš Castle">
        Spiš Castle
       </a>
       , (on the UNESCO list),
       <a href="/wiki/Orava_Castle" title="Orava Castle">
        Orava Castle
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava_Castle" title="Bratislava Castle">
        Bratislava Castle
       </a>
       , and the ruins of
       <a href="/wiki/Dev%C3%ADn_Castle" title="Devín Castle">
        Devín Castle
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/%C4%8Cachtice_Castle" title="Čachtice Castle">
        Čachtice Castle
       </a>
       was once the home of the world's most prolific female serial killer, the 'Bloody Lady',
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_B%C3%A1thory" title="Elizabeth Báthory">
        Elizabeth Báthory
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Slovakia's position in Europe and the country's past (part of the multicultural
       <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Hungary" title="Kingdom of Hungary">
        Kingdom of Hungary
       </a>
       , the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg" title="Habsburg">
        Habsburg
       </a>
       monarchy and
       <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">
        Czechoslovakia
       </a>
       ) made many cities and towns similar to the cities in the
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Republic" title="Czech Republic">
        Czech Republic
       </a>
       (such as
       <a href="/wiki/Prague" title="Prague">
        Prague
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">
        Austria
       </a>
       (such as
       <a href="/wiki/Salzburg" title="Salzburg">
        Salzburg
       </a>
       ) or
       <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">
        Hungary
       </a>
       (such as
       <a href="/wiki/Budapest" title="Budapest">
        Budapest
       </a>
       ). A historical center with at least one square has been preserved in many towns. Large historical centers can be found in
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
        Bratislava
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tren%C4%8D%C3%ADn" title="Trenčín">
        Trenčín
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="Košice">
        Košice
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica" title="Banská Štiavnica">
        Banská Štiavnica
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Levo%C4%8Da" title="Levoča">
        Levoča
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Trnava" title="Trnava">
        Trnava
       </a>
       . Historical centers have been going through restoration in recent years.
      </p>
      <p>
       Historical churches can be found in virtually every village and town in Slovakia. Most of them are built in the
       <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">
        Baroque
       </a>
       style, but there are also many examples of
       <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">
        Romanesque
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">
        Gothic architecture
       </a>
       , for example
       <a href="/wiki/Bansk%C3%A1_Bystrica" title="Banská Bystrica">
        Banská Bystrica
       </a>
       , Bardejov and
       <a href="/wiki/Spi%C5%A1sk%C3%A1_Kapitula" title="Spišská Kapitula">
        Spišská Kapitula
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Basilica_of_St._James,_Levo%C4%8Da" title="Basilica of St. James, Levoča">
        Basilica of St. James
       </a>
       in Levoča with the tallest wood-carved altar in the world and the Church of the Holy Spirit in
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDehra" title="Žehra">
        Žehra
       </a>
       with medieval
       <a href="/wiki/Fresco" title="Fresco">
        frescos
       </a>
       are UNESCO
       <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">
        World Heritage Sites
       </a>
       . The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Martin%27s_Concathedral" title="St. Martin's Concathedral">
        St. Martin's Concathedral
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
        Bratislava
       </a>
       served as the
       <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">
        coronation
       </a>
       church for the Kingdom of Hungary. The oldest sacral buildings in Slovakia stem from the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Moravia" title="Great Moravia">
        Great Moravian
       </a>
       period in the 9th century. Very precious structures are the complete wooden churches of northern and northern-eastern Slovakia. Most were built from the 15th century onwards by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catholic" title="Catholic">
        Catholics
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lutheran" title="Lutheran">
        Lutherans
       </a>
       and members of
       <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Christianity" title="Eastern Christianity">
        eastern-rite
       </a>
       churches.
      </p>
      <p>
       Typical souvenirs from Slovakia are dolls dressed in folk costumes, ceramic objects, crystal glass, carved wooden figures,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=%C4%8Crp%C3%A1k&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Črpák (page does not exist)">
        črpáks
       </a>
       (wooden pitchers),
       <a href="/wiki/Fujara" title="Fujara">
        fujaras
       </a>
       (a
       <a href="/wiki/Folk_instrument" title="Folk instrument">
        folk instrument
       </a>
       on the UNESCO list) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Vala%C5%A1ka" title="Valaška">
        valaškas
       </a>
       (a decorated folk hatchet) and above all products made from
       <a href="/wiki/Husk" title="Husk">
        corn husks
       </a>
       and wire, notably human figures. Souvenirs can be bought in the shops run by the state organisation ÚĽUV (
       <i>
        Ústredie ľudovej umeleckej výroby
       </i>
       – Centre of
       <a href="/wiki/Folk_art" title="Folk art">
        Folk Art
       </a>
       Production).
       <i>
        Dielo
       </i>
       shop chain sells works of Slovak artists and craftsmen. These shops are mostly found in towns and cities.
      </p>
      <p>
       Prices of imported products are generally the same as in the neighbouring countries, whereas prices of local products and services, especially food, are usually lower.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Science">
        Science
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Science">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
          </a>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          This section
          <b>
           does not
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">
            cite
           </a>
           any
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            sources
           </a>
          </b>
          .
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please help
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit">
            improve this section
           </a>
           by
           <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">
            adding citations to reliable sources
           </a>
           . Unsourced material may be challenged and
           <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">
            removed
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (November 2017)
           </i>
          </small>
          <small class="hide-when-compact">
           <i>
            (
            <a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">
             Learn how and when to remove this template message
            </a>
            )
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Academy_of_Sciences" title="Slovak Academy of Sciences">
        Slovak Academy of Sciences
       </a>
       has been the most important scientific and research institution in the country since 1953. Slovaks have made notable scientific and technical contributions during the history. The list of important scientists and their inventions include:
      </p>
      <ul>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Jozef_Murga%C5%A1" title="Jozef Murgaš">
         Jozef Murgaš
        </a>
        (1864–1929), contributed to development of
        <a href="/wiki/Wireless_telegraphy" title="Wireless telegraphy">
         wireless telegraphy
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107">
         <a href="#cite_note-107">
          [106]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Bah%C3%BD%C4%BE" title="Ján Bahýľ">
         Ján Bahýľ
        </a>
        (1856–1916), constructed the first motor-driven
        <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">
         helicopter
        </a>
        (four years before
        <a href="/wiki/Breguet_Aviation" title="Breguet Aviation">
         Bréguet
        </a>
        and
        <a href="/wiki/Paul_Cornu" title="Paul Cornu">
         Cornu
        </a>
        )
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108">
         <a href="#cite_note-108">
          [107]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0tefan_Bani%C4%8D" title="Štefan Banič">
         Štefan Banič
        </a>
        (1870–1941), constructed the first actively used parachute
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109">
         <a href="#cite_note-109">
          [108]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Aurel_Stodola" title="Aurel Stodola">
         Aurel Stodola
        </a>
        (1859–1942), created a bionic arm in 1916 and pioneered steam and gas
        <a href="/wiki/Turbine" title="Turbine">
         turbines
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110">
         <a href="#cite_note-110">
          [109]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/John_Dopyera" title="John Dopyera">
         John Dopyera
        </a>
        (1893–1988), constructed a
        <a href="/wiki/Resonator_guitar" title="Resonator guitar">
         resonator guitar
        </a>
        , an important contribution to the development of acoustic
        <a href="/wiki/String_instrument" title="String instrument">
         string instrument
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111">
         <a href="#cite_note-111">
          [110]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Eugene_Cernan" title="Eugene Cernan">
         Eugen Čerňan
        </a>
        (1934–2017), American astronaut of Slovak origin was the last man to visit the Moon
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Ivan_Bella" title="Ivan Bella">
         Ivan Bella
        </a>
        (1964), first Slovak in space,
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112">
         <a href="#cite_note-112">
          [111]
         </a>
        </sup>
        having participated in a 9-day joint Russian-French-Slovak mission on the
        <a href="/wiki/Space_station" title="Space station">
         space station
        </a>
        <a href="/wiki/Mir" title="Mir">
         Mir
        </a>
        in 1999.
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Carleton_Gajdusek" title="Daniel Carleton Gajdusek">
         Daniel Gajdusek
        </a>
        (1923–2008), (of Slovak ancestry) won the
        <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Prize" title="Nobel Prize">
         Nobel Prize
        </a>
        in Physiology or Medicine in 1976 for work on
        <a href="/wiki/Kuru_(disease)" title="Kuru (disease)">
         Kuru
        </a>
        <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113">
         <a href="#cite_note-113">
          [112]
         </a>
        </sup>
       </li>
      </ul>
      <p>
       Slovakia is currently in the negotiation process of becoming a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">
        European Space Agency
       </a>
       . Observer status was granted in 2010, when Slovakia signed the General Agreement on Cooperation
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114">
        <a href="#cite_note-114">
         [113]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in which information about ongoing education programmes was shared and Slovakia was invited to various negotiations of the ESA. In 2015, Slovakia signed the European Cooperating State Agreement based on which Slovakia committed to the finance entrance programme named PECS (Plan for the European Cooperating States) which serves as preparation for full membership. Slovak research and development organizations can apply for funding of projects regarding space technologies advancement. Full membership of Slovakia in the ESA is expected in 2020 after signing the ESA Convention. Slovakia will be obliged to set state budget inclusive ESA funding.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">

       </span>

      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:388px;max-width:388px">
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_2011_Ethnic.png">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="1100" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Slovakia_2011_Ethnic.png/190px-Slovakia_2011_Ethnic.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Slovakia_2011_Ethnic.png/285px-Slovakia_2011_Ethnic.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Slovakia_2011_Ethnic.png/380px-Slovakia_2011_Ethnic.png 2x" width="190"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          Ethnic makeup of Slovakia according to Census 2011
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Slovakia_2011_Language.png">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="595" data-file-width="1100" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Slovakia_2011_Language.png/190px-Slovakia_2011_Language.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Slovakia_2011_Language.png/285px-Slovakia_2011_Language.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/55/Slovakia_2011_Language.png/380px-Slovakia_2011_Language.png 2x" width="190"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          Linguistic makeup of Slovakia according to Census 2011
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       According to the 2011 census,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115">
        <a href="#cite_note-115">
         [114]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the majority of the inhabitants of Slovakia are
       <a href="/wiki/Slovaks" title="Slovaks">
        Slovaks
       </a>
       (80.7%).
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarians_in_Slovakia" title="Hungarians in Slovakia">
        Hungarians
       </a>
       are the largest
       <a href="/wiki/Minority_group" title="Minority group">
        ethnic minority
       </a>
       (8.5%). Other
       <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">
        ethnic groups
       </a>
       include
       <a href="/wiki/Romani_people" title="Romani people">
        Roma
       </a>
       (2%),
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116">
        <a href="#cite_note-116">
         [115]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Czechs" title="Czechs">
        Czechs
       </a>
       (0.6%),
       <a href="/wiki/Rusyns" title="Rusyns">
        Rusyns
       </a>
       (0.6%) and others or unspecified (7.6%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gov-stats_117-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-gov-stats-117">
         [116]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Unofficial estimates on the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roma_in_Slovakia" title="Roma in Slovakia">
        Roma
       </a>
       population are much higher, around 5.6%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118">
        <a href="#cite_note-118">
         [117]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2007 Slovakia was estimated to have a
       <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">
        total fertility rate
       </a>
       of 1.33
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cia_64-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-cia-64">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
       (i.e., the average woman will have 1.33 children in her lifetime), which is significantly below the
       <a href="/wiki/Sub-replacement_fertility" title="Sub-replacement fertility">
        replacement level
       </a>
       and is one of the lowest rates among
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Member_State_of_the_European_Union" title="Member State of the European Union">
        EU countries
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The largest waves of Slovak emigration occurred in the 19th and early 20th centuries. In the 1990 US census, 1.8 million people self-identified as having Slovak ancestry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119">
        <a href="#cite_note-119">
         [118]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">
        Languages
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Languages">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">
        Slovak language
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Slovak_language" title="History of the Slovak language">
        History of the Slovak language
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Slovak_alphabet.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="387" data-file-width="446" height="174" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Slovak_alphabet.png/200px-Slovak_alphabet.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Slovak_alphabet.png/300px-Slovak_alphabet.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/Slovak_alphabet.png/400px-Slovak_alphabet.png 2x" width="200"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Slovak_alphabet.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovak_alphabet" title="Slovak alphabet">
          Slovak alphabet
         </a>
         has 46 characters, of which 3 are
         <a href="/wiki/Digraph_(orthography)" title="Digraph (orthography)">
          digraphs
         </a>
         and 18 contain
         <a href="/wiki/Diacritic" title="Diacritic">
          diacritics
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">
        official language
       </a>
       is
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_language" title="Slovak language">
        Slovak
       </a>
       , a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Slavic_languages" title="Slavic languages">
        Slavic language family
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_language" title="Hungarian language">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       is widely spoken in the southern regions, and
       <a href="/wiki/Rusyn_language" title="Rusyn language">
        Rusyn
       </a>
       is used in some parts of the Northeast.
       <a href="/wiki/Minority_language" title="Minority language">
        Minority languages
       </a>
       hold co-official status in the municipalities in which the size of the minority population meets the legal threshold of 15% in two consecutive censuses.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120">
        <a href="#cite_note-120">
         [119]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Slovakia is ranked among the top EU countries regarding the knowledge of foreign languages. In 2007, 68% of the population aged from 25 to 64 years claimed to speak two or more foreign languages, finishing 2nd highest in the European Union. The best known foreign language in Slovakia is
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_language" title="Czech language">
        Czech
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">
        Eurostat
       </a>
       report also shows that 98.3% of Slovak students in the upper secondary education take on two foreign languages, ranking highly over the average 60.1% in the European Union.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121">
        <a href="#cite_note-121">
         [120]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The deaf community uses the
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Sign_Language" title="Slovak Sign Language">
        Slovak Sign Language
       </a>
       . Even though spoken Czech and Slovak are similar, the Slovak Sign language is not particularly close to
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_Sign_Language" title="Czech Sign Language">
        Czech Sign Language
       </a>
       .
      </p>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">

       <span class="mw-editsection">

        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Slovakia" title="Religion in Slovakia">

       </a>
      </div>

        History of Christianity in Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
