          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Elisabeth_Cathedral" title="St. Elisabeth Cathedral">
           St. Elisabeth Cathedral
          </a>
          in
          <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="Košice">
           Košice
          </a>
          is Slovakia's largest church
          <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122">
           <a href="#cite_note-122">
            [121]
           </a>
          </sup>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="float:left;margin:1px;width:116px;max-width:116px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Slavkovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt,_Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_(3).JPG">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="3356" data-file-width="2673" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Slavkovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt%2C_Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_%283%29.JPG/114px-Slavkovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt%2C_Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_%283%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Slavkovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt%2C_Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_%283%29.JPG/171px-Slavkovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt%2C_Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_%283%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/Slavkovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt%2C_Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_%283%29.JPG/228px-Slavkovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt%2C_Vysok%C3%A9_Tatry_%283%29.JPG 2x" width="114"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          Cross at the top of the
          <a href="/wiki/Slavkovsk%C3%BD_%C5%A1t%C3%ADt" title="Slavkovský štít">
           Slavkovský štít
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div style="clear:left">
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Slovakia" title="Constitution of Slovakia">
        Slovak constitution
       </a>
       guarantees
       <a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_religion" title="Freedom of religion">
        freedom of religion
       </a>
       . In 2011, 62.0% of Slovaks identified themselves as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" title="Roman Catholic">
        Roman Catholics
       </a>
       , 8.9% as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">
        Protestants
       </a>
       , 3.8% as
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Slovak Greek Catholic Church">
        Greek Catholics
       </a>
       , 0.9% as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orthodox_Christianity" title="Orthodox Christianity">
        Orthodox
       </a>
       , 13.4% identified themselves as
       <a href="/wiki/Atheism" title="Atheism">
        atheists
       </a>
       or non-religious, and 10.6% did not answer the question about their belief.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123">
        <a href="#cite_note-123">
         [122]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2004, about one third of the then church members regularly attended church services.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124">
        <a href="#cite_note-124">
         [123]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Greek_Catholic_Church" title="Slovak Greek Catholic Church">
        Slovak Greek Catholic Church
       </a>
       is an Eastern rite
       <a href="/wiki/Sui_iuris" title="Sui iuris">
        sui iuris
       </a>
       Catholic Church. The pre–World War II population of the country included an estimated 90,000 Jews (1.6% of the population). After the genocidal policies of the Nazi era, only about 2,300 Jews remain today (0.04% of the population).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125">
        <a href="#cite_note-125">
         [124]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In 2016, Slovak parliament passed a new bill that will obstruct
       <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">
        Islam
       </a>
       and other religious organisations from becoming state-recognised religion by doubling the minimum followers threshold from 25,000 to 50,000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126">
        <a href="#cite_note-126">
         [125]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The law passed by a two-third majority at the parliament. In 2010, there were an estimated 5,000
       <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">
        Muslims
       </a>
       in Slovakia representing less than 0.1% of the country's population.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127">
        <a href="#cite_note-127">
         [126]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Slovakia is the last member state of the European Union without a mosque.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128">
        <a href="#cite_note-128">
         [127]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Education">
        Education
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Education">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Slovakia" title="Education in Slovakia">
        Education in Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Education in Slovakia is compulsory from age 6 to 16. The education system consists of elementary school which is divided into two parts, the first grade(age 6–10) and the second grade(age 10–15) which is finished by taking nationwide testing called Monitor, from Slovak language and math. Parents may apply for social assistance for a child that is studying on an elementary school or a high-school. If approved, the state provides basic study necessities for the child. Schools provide books to all their students with usual exceptions of books for studying a foreign language and books which require taking notes in them, which are mostly present at the first grade of elementary school.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bratislava_09.03.2012_12-00-41.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2393" data-file-width="3580" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bratislava_09.03.2012_12-00-41.JPG/220px-Bratislava_09.03.2012_12-00-41.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bratislava_09.03.2012_12-00-41.JPG/330px-Bratislava_09.03.2012_12-00-41.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Bratislava_09.03.2012_12-00-41.JPG/440px-Bratislava_09.03.2012_12-00-41.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bratislava_09.03.2012_12-00-41.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comenius_University_in_Bratislava" title="Comenius University in Bratislava">
          Comenius University
         </a>
         headquarters in
         <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
          Bratislava
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After finishing elementary school, students are obliged to take one year in high school. They are able to pick from Gymnasium, which is seen as the highest level of high-school education and usually considered as a preparatory school for attending a university, although anyone can apply to any university. Besides Gymnasiums, Slovakia has specialised high schools with bacalaureat and specialised highschools without bacalaureat. Schools with bacalaureat take 5 years to complete while the ones without usually take less. Gymnasiums and many other high schools require passing an entry exam, consider previous study results or perform a combination of both before accepting a new student. A student may apply to two high schools at once. If student fails to get accepted in any high school, the student can submit an appeal or seek a third high school with an empty slot for one more student outside of the standard application process. Parents and students prefer to avoid this uncertainty and tend to choose at least one high school with a high chance of acceptance. Most high-schools are finished by passing a matura exam, which consists of Slovak language and literature, one foreign language and one specialised subject. If school offered multiple specializations or taught multiple foreign languages, student may choose which subject he or she wants to do the matura exam in. If student wants and the school allows it, it's possible to do matura exam in more than three subjects.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:EUBA3.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/EUBA3.jpg/220px-EUBA3.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/EUBA3.jpg/330px-EUBA3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/EUBA3.jpg/440px-EUBA3.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:EUBA3.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Main Building Hall of the
         <a href="/wiki/University_of_Economics_in_Bratislava" title="University of Economics in Bratislava">
          University of Economics
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       After finishing a high school, students can go to university and are highly encouraged to do so. Slovakia has a wide range of universities. The biggest university is
       <a href="/wiki/Comenius_University" title="Comenius University">
        Comenius University
       </a>
       , established in 1919. Although it's not the first university ever established on Slovak territory, it's the oldest university that is still running. Most universities in Slovakia are public funded, where anyone can apply. Every citizen has a right for free education on public schools. If student has to repeat a year or attends a second school after obtaining a degree, or is older than 26 years and attending Bachelor's or Master's courses or is older than 30 years and attending Doctorate's courses, student has to pay the expenses. Students of Doctorate's courses receive a scholarship. Students of Bachelor's and of Master's courses can apply for a scholarship depending on their study performance. The limit for applying for performance scholarship is set individually by each university.
      </p>
      <p>
       Slovakia has several privately funded universities, however public universities consistently score better in the ranking than their private counterparts. Universities have different criteria for accepting students. Anyone can apply to any number of universities. The limiting factor is the cost of application fees, which can range from a few € to over 100 € per one application. The student may apply for a social discount for the application fee. Several universities, including some the best ranking in Slovakia, accept all applicants and perform a screening process during the study, which results in a higher dropout rate among the students compared to universities that require passing an entry exam. Other methods of acceptance may include weighting past study results from high school, passing an entry test or a combination of both.
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Programme_for_International_Student_Assessment" title="Programme for International Student Assessment">
        Programme for International Student Assessment
       </a>
       , coordinated by the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Organisation_for_Economic_Co-operation_and_Development" title="Organisation for Economic Co-operation and Development">
        OECD
       </a>
       , currently ranks
       <a href="/wiki/Education_in_Slovakia" title="Education in Slovakia">
        Slovak secondary education
       </a>
       the 30th in the world (placing it just below the United States and just above Spain).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129">
        <a href="#cite_note-129">
         [128]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Slovakia" title="Culture of Slovakia">
        Culture of Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Folk_tradition">
        Folk tradition
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Folk tradition">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:2017_Bodru%C5%BEal,_cerkiew_%C5%9Bw._Miko%C5%82aja,_widok_ze_strony_po%C5%82udniowej.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2350" data-file-width="3679" height="141" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/2017_Bodru%C5%BEal%2C_cerkiew_%C5%9Bw._Miko%C5%82aja%2C_widok_ze_strony_po%C5%82udniowej.jpg/220px-2017_Bodru%C5%BEal%2C_cerkiew_%C5%9Bw._Miko%C5%82aja%2C_widok_ze_strony_po%C5%82udniowej.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/2017_Bodru%C5%BEal%2C_cerkiew_%C5%9Bw._Miko%C5%82aja%2C_widok_ze_strony_po%C5%82udniowej.jpg/330px-2017_Bodru%C5%BEal%2C_cerkiew_%C5%9Bw._Miko%C5%82aja%2C_widok_ze_strony_po%C5%82udniowej.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7f/2017_Bodru%C5%BEal%2C_cerkiew_%C5%9Bw._Miko%C5%82aja%2C_widok_ze_strony_po%C5%82udniowej.jpg/440px-2017_Bodru%C5%BEal%2C_cerkiew_%C5%9Bw._Miko%C5%82aja%2C_widok_ze_strony_po%C5%82udniowej.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:2017_Bodru%C5%BEal,_cerkiew_%C5%9Bw._Miko%C5%82aja,_widok_ze_strony_po%C5%82udniowej.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         This wooden church in
         <a href="/wiki/Bodru%C5%BEal" title="Bodružal">
          Bodružal
         </a>
         is an example of Rusyn folk architecture and is a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">
          UNESCO World Heritage Site
         </a>
         .
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Folk_tradition" title="Folk tradition">
        Folk tradition
       </a>
       has rooted strongly in Slovakia and is reflected in literature, music, dance and architecture. The prime example is a Slovak national anthem,
       <i>
        "
        <a href="/wiki/Nad_Tatrou_sa_bl%C3%BDska" title="Nad Tatrou sa blýska">
         Nad Tatrou sa blýska
        </a>
        "
       </i>
       , which is based on a melody from
       <i>
        "
        <a href="/wiki/Kopala_studienku" title="Kopala studienku">
         Kopala studienku
        </a>
        "
       </i>
       folk song.
      </p>
      <p>
       Manifestation of Slovak folklore culture is the "
       <i>
        Východná
       </i>
       " Folklore Festival. It is the oldest and largest nationwide festival with international participation,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130">
        <a href="#cite_note-130">
         [129]
        </a>
       </sup>
       which takes place in
       <a href="/wiki/V%C3%BDchodn%C3%A1" title="Východná">
        Východná
       </a>
       annually. Slovakia is usually represented by many groups but mainly by SĽUK (
       <i>
        Slovenský ľudový umelecký kolektív – Slovak folk art collective
       </i>
       ). SĽUK is the largest Slovak folk art group, trying to preserve the folklore tradition.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hontianska_parada_2003-DSC01152.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2560" data-file-width="1920" height="200" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Hontianska_parada_2003-DSC01152.JPG/150px-Hontianska_parada_2003-DSC01152.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Hontianska_parada_2003-DSC01152.JPG/225px-Hontianska_parada_2003-DSC01152.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Hontianska_parada_2003-DSC01152.JPG/300px-Hontianska_parada_2003-DSC01152.JPG 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hontianska_parada_2003-DSC01152.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Slovak women in traditional dress demonstrating a traditional method of grinding grain into flour
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       An example of wooden folk architecture in Slovakia can be seen in the well preserved village of
       <a href="/wiki/Vlkol%C3%ADnec" title="Vlkolínec">
        Vlkolínec
       </a>
       which has been the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">
        UNESCO World Heritage Site
       </a>
       since 1993.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131">
        <a href="#cite_note-131">
         [130]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Pre%C5%A1ov_Region" title="Prešov Region">
        Prešov Region
       </a>
       preserves the world's most remarkable folk wooden churches. Most of them are protected by Slovak law as
       <a href="/wiki/Cultural_heritage" title="Cultural heritage">
        cultural heritage
       </a>
       , but some of them are on the
       <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">
        UNESCO
       </a>
       list too, in Bodružal, Hervartov, Ladomirová and Ruská Bystrá.
      </p>
      <p>
       The best known Slovak hero, found in many folk
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mythologies" title="Mythologies">
        mythologies
       </a>
       , is
       <a href="/wiki/Juraj_J%C3%A1no%C5%A1%C3%ADk" title="Juraj Jánošík">
        Juraj Jánošík
       </a>
       (1688–1713) (the Slovak equivalent of
       <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood" title="Robin Hood">
        Robin Hood
       </a>
       ). The legend says he was taking from the rich and giving to the poor. Jánošík's life was depicted in a list of literature works and many movies throughout the 20th century. One of the most popular is a
       <a href="/wiki/Film" title="Film">
        film
       </a>
       <i>
        Jánošík
       </i>
       directed by
       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Fri%C4%8D" title="Martin Frič">
        Martin Frič
       </a>
       in 1935.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132">
        <a href="#cite_note-132">
         [131]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Art">
        Art
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Art">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Visual_art" title="Visual art">
        Visual art
       </a>
       in Slovakia is represented through
       <a href="/wiki/Painting" title="Painting">
        painting
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Drawing" title="Drawing">
        drawing
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Printmaking" title="Printmaking">
        printmaking
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Illustration" title="Illustration">
        illustration
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Handicraft" title="Handicraft">
        arts and crafts
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">
        sculpture
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Photography" title="Photography">
        photography
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Conceptual_art" title="Conceptual art">
        conceptual art
       </a>
       . The supreme and central gallery institution displaying Slovak art nowadays is the
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_National_Gallery" title="Slovak National Gallery">
        Slovak National Gallery
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133">
        <a href="#cite_note-133">
         [132]
        </a>
       </sup>
       established in 1949.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Medieval time
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Master_MS_Birth_of_Jesus_(1500-1510).jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1198" data-file-width="768" height="203" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Master_MS_Birth_of_Jesus_%281500-1510%29.jpg/130px-Master_MS_Birth_of_Jesus_%281500-1510%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Master_MS_Birth_of_Jesus_%281500-1510%29.jpg/195px-Master_MS_Birth_of_Jesus_%281500-1510%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Master_MS_Birth_of_Jesus_%281500-1510%29.jpg/260px-Master_MS_Birth_of_Jesus_%281500-1510%29.jpg 2x" width="130"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Master_MS_Birth_of_Jesus_(1500-1510).jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/The_Visitation_(MS)" title="The Visitation (MS)">
          The Visitation
         </a>
         is a 1506 panel painting by
         <a href="/wiki/Master_MS" title="Master MS">
          Majster M. S.
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Well-known sculptor of the 15th century Late
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_art" title="Gothic art">
        Gothic
       </a>
       era in Slovakia is the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Master_Paul_of_Levo%C4%8Da" title="Master Paul of Levoča">
         Master Paul of Levoča
        </a>
       </i>
       . Although his work can be found in many places (
       <a href="/wiki/Bansk%C3%A1_Bystrica" title="Banská Bystrica">
        Banská Bystrica
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spi%C5%A1sk%C3%A1_Sobota" title="Spišská Sobota">
        Spišská Sobota
       </a>
       or Lomnička), his most famous is a wooden
       <a href="/wiki/Altar" title="Altar">
        altar
       </a>
       in the Church of St. Jacob in
       <a href="/wiki/Levo%C4%8Da" title="Levoča">
        Levoča
       </a>
       . With its height of 18.62 metres (61 ft), it is the tallest Gothic altar in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134">
        <a href="#cite_note-134">
         [133]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Well-known painters of that time are the
       <i>
        Master from Okoličné
       </i>
       , author of the altar in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/St._Elisabeth_Cathedral" title="St. Elisabeth Cathedral">
        St. Elisabeth Cathedral
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="Košice">
        Košice
       </a>
       , and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Master_MS" title="Master MS">
         Master M.S.
        </a>
       </i>
       of the 16th century, whose statue of Madonna can be seen in the Saint Catherine Church in
       <a href="/wiki/Bansk%C3%A1_%C5%A0tiavnica" title="Banská Štiavnica">
        Banská Štiavnica
       </a>
       . The statues of Saint Catherine and Saint Barbara are in the art gallery of the Slovak Mining Museum in Banská Štiavnica.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        19th century
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The 19th century in Slovakia was a turbulent period of time when Slovaks began experiencing their national revival in the kingdom of
       <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">
        Austria-Hungary
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">
        Romanticism
       </a>
       of
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jozef_B._Klemens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jozef B. Klemens (page does not exist)">
        Jozef B. Klemens
       </a>
       (1817–1883) and
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Michal_Boh%C3%BA%C5%88" title="Peter Michal Bohúň">
        Peter Michal Bohúň
       </a>
       (1822–1879) was represented in the portrait paintings of Slovak national protagonists of that time (Štefan Moyses,
       <a href="/wiki/Andrej_Sl%C3%A1dkovi%C4%8D" title="Andrej Sládkovič">
        Andrej Sládkovič
       </a>
       , Karol Kuzmány or
       <a href="/wiki/%C4%BDudov%C3%ADt_%C5%A0t%C3%BAr" title="Ľudovít Štúr">
        Ľudovít Štúr
       </a>
       ), depicting the revolutionary atmosphere of the 1840s in the background. Other important painters of the 19th century were mainly
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Portraitist" title="Portraitist">
        portraitists
       </a>
       Vojtech Angyal, Dominik Skutecký (1849–1921), J. Štetka, E. Ballo, Jozef Hanula (1863–1944),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Landscapist" title="Landscapist">
        landscapist
       </a>
       Karol Miloslav Lehotský (1846–1915) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impressionist" title="Impressionist">
        impressionists
       </a>
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Maximili%C3%A1n_Schurmann&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Maximilián Schurmann (page does not exist)">
        Maximilián Schurmann
       </a>
       (1863–1944) and P. Kern.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Sculpture" title="Sculpture">
        Sculpture
       </a>
       in the 19th century was dominated by a sacral sculptor Vavrinec Dunajský (1784–1833) and his son Ladislav Dunajský, author of
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Holl%C3%BD" title="Ján Hollý">
        Ján Hollý
       </a>
       memorial in
       <a href="/wiki/Dobr%C3%A1_Voda,_Trnava_District" title="Dobrá Voda, Trnava District">
        Dobrá Voda
       </a>
       . Another important sculptors were
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=J%C3%A1n_Koniarek&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ján Koniarek (page does not exist)">
        Ján Koniarek
       </a>
       (1878–1952),
       <a href="/wiki/Alajos_Str%C3%B3bl" title="Alajos Stróbl">
        Alajos Stróbl
       </a>
       (1856–1926),
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1nos_Fadrusz" title="János Fadrusz">
        János Fadrusz
       </a>
       (1858–1903) and
       <a href="/wiki/Alojz_Rigele" title="Alojz Rigele">
        Alojz Rigele
       </a>
       (1879–1940).
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        20th century
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:132px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:150px-Mother_Galanda.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="500" data-file-width="410" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/150px-Mother_Galanda.jpg/130px-150px-Mother_Galanda.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/150px-Mother_Galanda.jpg/195px-150px-Mother_Galanda.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/150px-Mother_Galanda.jpg/260px-150px-Mother_Galanda.jpg 2x" width="130"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:150px-Mother_Galanda.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Mikul%C3%A1%C5%A1_Galanda" title="Mikuláš Galanda">
          Mikuláš Galanda
         </a>
         –
         <i>
          Mother
         </i>
         (1933)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Painters
       <a href="/wiki/Mikul%C3%A1%C5%A1_Galanda" title="Mikuláš Galanda">
        Mikuláš Galanda
       </a>
       (1895–1938),
       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Benka" title="Martin Benka">
        Martin Benka
       </a>
       (1888–1971),
       <a href="/wiki/Janko_Alexy" title="Janko Alexy">
        Janko Alexy
       </a>
       (1894–1970),
       <a href="/wiki/Milo%C5%A1_Alexander_Bazovsk%C3%BD" title="Miloš Alexander Bazovský">
        Miloš Alexander Bazovský
       </a>
       (1899–1968),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Gust%C3%A1v_Mall%C3%BD&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Gustáv Mallý (page does not exist)">
        Gustáv Mallý
       </a>
       (1879–1952) and
       <a href="/wiki/Jan_H%C3%A1la" title="Jan Hála">
        Jan Hála
       </a>
       (1890–1959) are considered to be the ones who laid foundations of the Slovak
       <a href="/wiki/Modern_art" title="Modern art">
        modern art
       </a>
       in the first half of the 20th century. The inspiration of their work stems mainly from the lives of everyday people in Slovak
       <a href="/wiki/Rural_area" title="Rural area">
        rurals
       </a>
       which they admired and idealised. The painters influenced by
       <a href="/wiki/Art_Nouveau" title="Art Nouveau">
        Art Nouveau
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Symbolism_(arts)" title="Symbolism (arts)">
        symbolism
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Expressionism" title="Expressionism">
        expressionism
       </a>
       are Zolo Palugyay (1898–1935), Anton Jasusch (1882–1965),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Edmund_Gwerk&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Edmund Gwerk (page does not exist)">
        Edmund Gwerk
       </a>
       (1895–1956) or
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BAlius_Jakoby" title="Július Jakoby">
        Július Jakoby
       </a>
       (1903–1985). Important also is
       <a href="/wiki/Bla%C5%BEej_Bal%C3%A1%C5%BE" title="Blažej Baláž">
        Blažej Baláž
       </a>
       (1958).
      </p>
      <p>
       Some of the most distinguished Slovak artists, whose work was closely linked to modern European art streams are
       <a href="/wiki/Koloman_Sokol" title="Koloman Sokol">
        Koloman Sokol
       </a>
       (1902–2003), who became a professor of graphic techniques at the
       <i>
        Escuela de las Artes del Libro
       </i>
       and at the University of
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico_City" title="Mexico City">
        Mexico City
       </a>
       from 1937 to 1941,
       <a href="/wiki/%C4%BDudov%C3%ADt_Fulla" title="Ľudovít Fulla">
        Ľudovít Fulla
       </a>
       (1902–1980) who received many international prices for his work
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135">
        <a href="#cite_note-135">
         [134]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Imro_Weiner-Kr%C3%A1%C4%BE&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Imro Weiner-Kráľ (page does not exist)">
        Imro Weiner-Kráľ
       </a>
       (1901–1978). The generation of 1909 is represented by
       <a href="/wiki/Cypri%C3%A1n_Majern%C3%ADk" title="Cyprián Majerník">
        Cyprián Majerník
       </a>
       (1909–1945), Ján Želibský,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=J%C3%A1n_Mudroch&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ján Mudroch (page does not exist)">
        Ján Mudroch
       </a>
       (1909–1968), Ladislav Čemický (1909–1968) and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ester_M._%C5%A0imerov%C3%A1&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ester M. Šimerová (page does not exist)">
        Ester M. Šimerová
       </a>
       (1909).
      </p>
      <p>
       Slovak
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graphic_art" title="Graphic art">
        graphic art
       </a>
       experienced its peak during the 20th century. The most notable print-makers are
       <a href="/wiki/Koloman_Sokol" title="Koloman Sokol">
        Koloman Sokol
       </a>
       (1902–2003),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vincent_Hlo%C5%BEn%C3%ADk&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vincent Hložník (page does not exist)">
        Vincent Hložník
       </a>
       (1919–1997),
       <a href="/wiki/Alb%C3%ADn_Brunovsk%C3%BD" title="Albín Brunovský">
        Albín Brunovský
       </a>
       (1935–1997),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jozef_Jankovi%C4%8D&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jozef Jankovič (page does not exist)">
        Jozef Jankovič
       </a>
       (1937),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Du%C5%A1an_K%C3%A1llay&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Dušan Kállay (page does not exist)">
        Dušan Kállay
       </a>
       (1948),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Vladim%C3%ADr_Ga%C5%BEovi%C4%8D&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Vladimír Gažovič (page does not exist)">
        Vladimír Gažovič
       </a>
       (1939),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Karol_Ondrei%C4%8Dka&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Karol Ondreička (page does not exist)">
        Karol Ondreička
       </a>
       (1944–2003)
       <a href="/wiki/Bla%C5%BEej_Bal%C3%A1%C5%BE" title="Blažej Baláž">
        Blažej Baláž
       </a>
       (1958) or the young generation of artists Katarína Vavrová, and Matej Krén.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Medzilaborce-1.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2352" data-file-width="3136" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Medzilaborce-1.jpg/220px-Medzilaborce-1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Medzilaborce-1.jpg/330px-Medzilaborce-1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Medzilaborce-1.jpg/440px-Medzilaborce-1.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Medzilaborce-1.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol_Museum_of_Modern_Art" title="Andy Warhol Museum of Modern Art">
          Andy Warhol Museum of Modern Art
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Medzilaborce" title="Medzilaborce">
          Medzilaborce
         </a>
         .
         <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">
          Andy Warhol
         </a>
         's parents were immigrants from Slovakia.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Andy_Warhol" title="Andy Warhol">
        Andy Warhol
       </a>
       (1928–1987), a leading figure in the 20th century
       <a href="/wiki/Art_movement" title="Art movement">
        visual art movement
       </a>
       known as
       <a href="/wiki/Pop_art" title="Pop art">
        pop art
       </a>
       , was born in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pittsburgh,_Pennsylvania" title="Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania">
        Pittsburgh, Pennsylvania
       </a>
       as
       <i>
        Andrej Varchola
       </i>
       to Slovak parents Ondrej Varchola (1889–1942) and
       <a href="/wiki/Julia_Warhola" title="Julia Warhola">
        Júlia
       </a>
       (née Zavacká, 1892–1972).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136">
        <a href="#cite_note-136">
         [135]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A museum dedicated to him is in
       <a href="/wiki/Medzilaborce" title="Medzilaborce">
        Medzilaborce
       </a>
       , where his parents lived.
      </p>
      <p>
       Notable Slovak
       <a href="/wiki/Photography" title="Photography">
        photographers
       </a>
       in the 20th century are
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Martin%C4%8Dek&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Martin Martinček (page does not exist)">
        Martin Martinček
       </a>
       (1913–2004) and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Karol_K%C3%A1llay&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Karol Kállay (page does not exist)">
        Karol Kállay
       </a>
       (1926–2012). Both Martinček and Kállay received the EFIAP (Excellence de la Fédération Internationale de l' Art Photographique) price in 1970.
      </p>
      <p>
       Sculpture in the 20th century is represented by
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=J%C3%A1n_Koniarek&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ján Koniarek (page does not exist)">
        Ján Koniarek
       </a>
       (1878–1952),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=J%C3%BAlius_B%C3%A1rtfay&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Július Bártfay (page does not exist)">
        Július Bártfay
       </a>
       (1888–1979),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tibor_B%C3%A1rtfay&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tibor Bártfay (page does not exist)">
        Tibor Bártfay
       </a>
       (1922) Ján Mathé (1922),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Jozef_Kostka&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Jozef Kostka (page does not exist)">
        Jozef Kostka
       </a>
       (1912–1996),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Ladislav_Snopek&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Ladislav Snopek (page does not exist)">
        Ladislav Snopek
       </a>
       (1919–2010), Rudolf Uher or Rudolf Hornák.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        21st century
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Notable Slovak artists of the 21st century include
       <a href="/wiki/Cyril_Bla%C5%BEo" title="Cyril Blažo">
        Cyril Blažo
       </a>
       (1970), and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Viliam_Loviska" title="Viliam Loviska">
        Viliam Loviska
       </a>
       (1964)
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
        Literature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Literature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Further information:
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_literature" title="Slovak literature">
        Slovak literature
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:152px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1743" data-file-width="1236" height="212" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg/150px-Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg/225px-Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg/300px-Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg 2x" width="150"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Bozetech_Klemens_Stur.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/%C4%BDudov%C3%ADt_%C5%A0t%C3%BAr" title="Ľudovít Štúr">
          Ľudovít Štúr
         </a>
         , the author of the Slovak language standard
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       For a list of notable Slovak writers and poets, see
       <a href="/wiki/Lists_of_Slovak_authors" title="Lists of Slovak authors">
        List of Slovak authors
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Christian topics include: poem
       <a href="/wiki/Proglas" title="Proglas">
        Proglas
       </a>
       as a foreword to the four
       <a href="/wiki/Gospel" title="Gospel">
        Gospels
       </a>
       , partial translations of the Bible into
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Church_Slavonic" title="Old Church Slavonic">
        Old Church Slavonic
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        Zakon sudnyj ljudem
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Medieval_literature" title="Medieval literature">
        Medieval literature
       </a>
       , in the period from the 11th to the 15th centuries, was written in
       <a href="/wiki/Latin" title="Latin">
        Latin
       </a>
       , Czech and Slovakised Czech. Lyric (prayers, songs and formulas) was still controlled by the Church, while epic was concentrated on legends. Authors from this period include
       <a href="/wiki/Johannes_de_Thurocz" title="Johannes de Thurocz">
        Johannes de Thurocz
       </a>
       , author of the
       <a href="/wiki/Chronica_Hungarorum" title="Chronica Hungarorum">
        Chronica Hungarorum
       </a>
       and Maurus, both of them Hungarians.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Phillips_137-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Phillips-137">
         [136]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The worldly literature also emerged and chronicles were written in this period.
      </p>
      <p>
       There were two leading persons who codified the Slovak language. The first was
       <a href="/wiki/Anton_Bernol%C3%A1k" title="Anton Bernolák">
        Anton Bernolák
       </a>
       whose concept was based on the western Slovak
       <a href="/wiki/Dialect" title="Dialect">
        dialect
       </a>
       in 1787. It was the codification of the first ever literary language of Slovaks. The second was
       <a href="/wiki/%C4%BDudov%C3%ADt_%C5%A0t%C3%BAr" title="Ľudovít Štúr">
        Ľudovít Štúr
       </a>
       , whose formation of the Slovak language took principles from the central Slovak dialect in 1843.
      </p>
      <p>
       Slovakia is also known for its polyhistors, of whom include
       <a href="/wiki/Pavel_Jozef_%C5%A0af%C3%A1rik" title="Pavel Jozef Šafárik">
        Pavol Jozef Šafárik
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Matthias_Bel" title="Matthias Bel">
        Matej Bel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Koll%C3%A1r" title="Ján Kollár">
        Ján Kollár
       </a>
       , and its political revolutionaries and reformists, such
       <a href="/wiki/Milan_Rastislav_%C5%A0tef%C3%A1nik" title="Milan Rastislav Štefánik">
        Milan Rastislav Štefánik
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Dub%C4%8Dek" title="Alexander Dubček">
        Alexander Dubček
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Famous globetrotter and explorer, count
       <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Benyovszky" title="Maurice Benyovszky">
        Móric Benyovszky
       </a>
       had Slovak ancestors.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Slovakia" title="Music of Slovakia">
        Music of Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>

          </a>
         </div>

         </div>

          <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
           Bratislava
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
        <div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:192px;max-width:192px">
         <div class="thumbimage">
          <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Kosice_(Slovakia)_-_State_Theater_5.jpg">
           <img alt="" data-file-height="1920" data-file-width="2560" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kosice_%28Slovakia%29_-_State_Theater_5.jpg/190px-Kosice_%28Slovakia%29_-_State_Theater_5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kosice_%28Slovakia%29_-_State_Theater_5.jpg/285px-Kosice_%28Slovakia%29_-_State_Theater_5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Kosice_%28Slovakia%29_-_State_Theater_5.jpg/380px-Kosice_%28Slovakia%29_-_State_Theater_5.jpg 2x" width="190"/>
          </a>
         </div>
         <div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">
          <a href="/wiki/State_Theatre_Ko%C5%A1ice" title="State Theatre Košice">
           State Theatre Košice
          </a>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Classical music
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The most important Slovak composers have been
       <a href="/wiki/Eugen_Sucho%C5%88" title="Eugen Suchoň">
        Eugen Suchoň
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mikul%C3%A1%C5%A1_Schneider-Trnavsk%C3%BD" title="Mikuláš Schneider-Trnavský">
        Mikuláš Schneider-Trnavský
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Cikker" title="Ján Cikker">
        Ján Cikker
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Levoslav_Bella" title="Ján Levoslav Bella">
        Ján Levoslav Bella
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Moyzes" title="Alexander Moyzes">
        Alexander Moyzes
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Dezider_Kardo%C5%A1" title="Dezider Kardoš">
        Dezider Kardoš
       </a>
       , in the 21st century
       <a href="/wiki/Vladim%C3%ADr_God%C3%A1r" title="Vladimír Godár">
        Vladimír Godár
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Machajd%C3%ADk" title="Peter Machajdík">
        Peter Machajdík
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Pop music
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Popular_music" title="Popular music">
        Popular music
       </a>
       began to replace
       <a href="/wiki/Folk_music" title="Folk music">
        folk music
       </a>
       beginning in the 1950s, when Slovakia was still part of
       <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">
        Czechoslovakia
       </a>
       ; American
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
        jazz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">
        R&amp;B
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">
        rock and roll
       </a>
       were popular, alongside
       <a href="/wiki/Waltz" title="Waltz">
        waltzes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Polka" title="Polka">
        polkas
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Cs%C3%A1rd%C3%A1s" title="Csárdás">
        czardas
       </a>
       , among other folk forms. By the end of the 1950s, radios were common household items, though only state stations were legal. Slovak popular music began as a mix of
       <a href="/wiki/Bossa_nova" title="Bossa nova">
        bossa nova
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cool_jazz" title="Cool jazz">
        cool jazz
       </a>
       , and rock, with
       <a href="/wiki/Propaganda" title="Propaganda">
        propagandistic
       </a>
       lyrics. Dissenters listened to
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/%C3%96sterreichischer_Rundfunk" title="Österreichischer Rundfunk">
        ORF
       </a>
       (Austrian Radio),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Radio_Luxemburg" title="Radio Luxemburg">
        Radio Luxembourg
       </a>
       , or
       <a href="/wiki/Radio_Free_Europe/Radio_Liberty" title="Radio Free Europe/Radio Liberty">
        Slobodná Európa
       </a>
       (Radio Free Europe), which played more rock.
      </p>
      <p>
       Due to Czechoslovak isolation, the
       <a href="/wiki/Domestic_market" title="Domestic market">
        domestic market
       </a>
       was active and many original bands evolved. Slovakia had a very strong
       <a href="/wiki/Popular_culture" title="Popular culture">
        pop culture
       </a>
       during the 1970s and 1980s. This movement brought many original bands with their own unique interpretations of modern music. The quality of socialist music was very high. Stars such as
       <a href="/wiki/Karel_Gott" title="Karel Gott">
        Karel Gott
       </a>
       , Olympic, Pražský výběr (from the Czech Republic) or
       <a href="/wiki/El%C3%A1n_(band)" title="Elán (band)">
        Elán
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Modus_(band)" title="Modus (band)">
        Modus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tublatanka" title="Tublatanka">
        Tublatanka
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TEAM_(Slovak_band)" title="TEAM (Slovak band)">
        Team
       </a>
       (from Slovakia) and many others were highly acclaimed and many recorded their LPs in
       <a href="/wiki/Foreign_language" title="Foreign language">
        foreign languages
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       After the
       <a href="/wiki/Velvet_Revolution" title="Velvet Revolution">
        Velvet Revolution
       </a>
       and the declaration of the Slovak state, domestic music dramatically diversified as
       <a href="/wiki/Capitalism" title="Capitalism">
        free enterprise
       </a>
       encouraged the formation of new bands and the development of new
       <a href="/wiki/Music_genre" title="Music genre">
        genres of music
       </a>
       . Soon, however, major
       <a href="/wiki/Label" title="Label">
        labels
       </a>
       brought pop music to Slovakia and drove many of the small companies out of business. During the 1990s, American
       <a href="/wiki/Grunge" title="Grunge">
        grunge
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Alternative_rock" title="Alternative rock">
        alternative rock
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Britpop" title="Britpop">
        Britpop
       </a>
       have a wide following, as well as a newfound enthusiasm for musicals.
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Jazz
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Lipa" title="Peter Lipa">
        Peter Lipa
       </a>
       (born 1943) is a well-known Slovak singer, composer and promoter of modern
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
        jazz
       </a>
       . He is one of the main organisers of the "
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava_Jazz_Days" title="Bratislava Jazz Days">
        Bratislava Jazz Days
       </a>
       " festival, which takes place in the capital city at the end of October each year since 1975. It is the biggest jazz venue in Slovakia.
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Valihora" title="Martin Valihora">
        Martin Valihora
       </a>
       (1976), having been awarded a scholarship on the
       <a href="/wiki/Berklee_College_of_Music" title="Berklee College of Music">
        Berklee College of Music
       </a>
       in Boston,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138">
        <a href="#cite_note-138">
         [137]
        </a>
       </sup>
       he established himself as a part of the New York's jazz scene. He has been playing with the world's famous Japanese jazz
       <a href="/wiki/Pianist" title="Pianist">
        pianist
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Hiromi_Uehara" title="Hiromi Uehara">
        Hiromi Uehara
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139">
        <a href="#cite_note-139">
         [138]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Other notable Slovak jazz players are
       <a href="/wiki/Laco_D%C3%A9czi" title="Laco Déczi">
        Laco Déczi
       </a>
       (1938) – composer, jazz trumpeter,
       <a href="/wiki/Mari%C3%A1n_Varga" title="Marián Varga">
        Marián Varga
       </a>
       (1947-2017) – composer, organ player
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">
        Cuisine
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Cuisine">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_cuisine" title="Slovak cuisine">
        Slovak cuisine
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_wine" title="Slovak wine">
        Slovak wine
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Beer_in_Slovakia" title="Beer in Slovakia">
        Beer in Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Halusky_kapustnica.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="640" data-file-width="640" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Halusky_kapustnica.jpg/220px-Halusky_kapustnica.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Halusky_kapustnica.jpg/330px-Halusky_kapustnica.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Halusky_kapustnica.jpg/440px-Halusky_kapustnica.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Halusky_kapustnica.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Halu%C5%A1ky" title="Halušky">
          Halušky
         </a>
         with
         <a href="/wiki/Bryndza" title="Bryndza">
          bryndza
         </a>
         cheese,
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sourkrawt" title="Sourkrawt">
          kapustnica
         </a>
         soup and Zlatý Bažant dark beer – examples of Slovak cuisine
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Traditional Slovak cuisine is based mainly on
       <a href="/wiki/Pork" title="Pork">
        pork
       </a>
       meat,
       <a href="/wiki/Poultry" title="Poultry">
        poultry
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Chicken" title="Chicken">
        chicken
       </a>
       is the most widely eaten, followed by
       <a href="/wiki/Duck" title="Duck">
        duck
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Goose" title="Goose">
        goose
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Turkey_(bird)" title="Turkey (bird)">
        turkey
       </a>
       ),
       <a href="/wiki/Flour" title="Flour">
        flour
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Potato" title="Potato">
        potatoes
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cabbage" title="Cabbage">
        cabbage
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Milk_products" title="Milk products">
        milk products
       </a>
       . It is relatively closely related to
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_cuisine" title="Hungarian cuisine">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Czech_cuisine" title="Czech cuisine">
        Czech
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Austrian_cuisine" title="Austrian cuisine">
        Austrian cuisine
       </a>
       . On the east it is also influenced by
       <a href="/wiki/Ukrainian_cuisine" title="Ukrainian cuisine">
        Ukrainian
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Polish_cuisine" title="Polish cuisine">
        Polish cuisine
       </a>
       . In comparison with other European countries,
       <a href="/wiki/Game_(hunting)" title="Game (hunting)">
        "game meat"
       </a>
       is more accessible in Slovakia due to vast resources of forest and because hunting is relatively popular.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-EuropeNations2000_140-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-EuropeNations2000-140">
         [139]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boar" title="Boar">
        Boar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rabbit" title="Rabbit">
        rabbit
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Venison" title="Venison">
        venison
       </a>
       , are generally available throughout the year.
       <a href="/wiki/Sheep" title="Sheep">
        Lamb
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Goat" title="Goat">
        goat
       </a>
       are eaten but are not widely popular.
      </p>
      <p>
       The traditional Slovak meals are
       <a href="/wiki/Bryndzov%C3%A9_halu%C5%A1ky" title="Bryndzové halušky">
        bryndzové halušky
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Bryndzov%C3%A9_pirohy&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Bryndzové pirohy (page does not exist)">
        bryndzové pirohy
       </a>
       and other meals with potato dough and
       <a href="/wiki/Bryndza" title="Bryndza">
        bryndza
       </a>
       . Bryndza is a salty cheese made of a sheep milk, characterised by a strong taste and aroma. Bryndzové halušky must be on the menu of every traditional Slovak restaurant.
      </p>
      <p>
       A typical soup is a
       <a href="/wiki/Sauerkraut" title="Sauerkraut">
        sauerkraut
       </a>
       soup ("kapustnica"). A
       <a href="/wiki/Black_pudding" title="Black pudding">
        blood sausage
       </a>
       called "krvavnica", made from any and all parts of a butchered pig is also a specific Slovak meal.
      </p>
      <p>
       Wine is enjoyed throughout Slovakia.
       <a href="/wiki/Slovak_wine" title="Slovak wine">
        Slovak wine
       </a>
       comes predominantly from the southern areas along the Danube and its tributaries; the northern half of the country is too cold and mountainous to grow grapevines. Traditionally, white wine was more popular than red or rosé (except in some regions), and
       <a href="/wiki/Sweetness_of_wine" title="Sweetness of wine">
        sweet wine
       </a>
       more popular than dry, but in recent years tastes seem to be changing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141">
        <a href="#cite_note-141">
         [140]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Beer (mainly of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pilsener" title="Pilsener">
        pilsener
       </a>
       style, though
       <a href="/wiki/Dunkel" title="Dunkel">
        dark lagers
       </a>
       are also consumed) is also popular.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">
        Sport
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: Sport">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Slovakia" title="Sport in Slovakia">
        Sport in Slovakia
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Sport activities are practised widely in Slovakia, many of them on a professional level.
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">
        Ice hockey
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        football
       </a>
       have traditionally been regarded as the most popular sports in Slovakia. Among the popular are also
       <a href="/wiki/Tennis" title="Tennis">
        tennis
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Team_handball" title="Team handball">
        handball
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">
        basketball
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Volleyball" title="Volleyball">
        volleyball
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Whitewater_slalom" title="Whitewater slalom">
        whitewater slalom
       </a>
       or
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Athletics_(sport)" title="Athletics (sport)">
        athletics
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Ice Hockey
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1280" data-file-width="1920" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg/220px-Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg/330px-Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg/440px-Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Slovakia2010WinterOlympicscelebration2.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         The Slovak national ice hockey team celebrating a victory against
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swedish_national_men%27s_ice_hockey_team" title="Swedish national men's ice hockey team">
          Sweden
         </a>
         at the
         <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">
          2010 Winter Olympics
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       One of the most popular team sports in Slovakia is
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">
        ice hockey
       </a>
       . Slovakia became the member of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/IIHF" title="IIHF">
        IIHF
       </a>
       on 2 February 1993
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142">
        <a href="#cite_note-142">
         [141]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and ever since has won 4 medals in
       <a href="/wiki/Ice_Hockey_World_Championships" title="Ice Hockey World Championships">
        Ice Hockey World Championships
       </a>
       , consisting of 1 gold, 2 silver and 1 bronze medal. The most recent success is a silver medal from
       <a href="/wiki/2012_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2012 IIHF World Championship">
        2012 IIHF World Championship
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Helsinki" title="Helsinki">
        Helsinki
       </a>
       . Slovak national hockey team made five appearances in the Olympic games too, ended up 4th in the
       <a href="/wiki/2010_Winter_Olympics" title="2010 Winter Olympics">
        2010 Winter Olympics
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">
        Vancouver
       </a>
       . The country has 8280 registered players and is ranked 7th in the
       <a href="/wiki/IIHF_World_Ranking" title="IIHF World Ranking">
        IIHF World Ranking
       </a>
       at present. Prior to 2012, Slovak team
       <a href="/wiki/HC_Slovan_Bratislava" title="HC Slovan Bratislava">
        HC Slovan Bratislava
       </a>
       joined the
       <a href="/wiki/Kontinental_Hockey_League" title="Kontinental Hockey League">
        Kontinental Hockey League
       </a>
       , considered the strongest hockey league in Europe, and the second-best in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143">
        <a href="#cite_note-143">
         [142]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Slovakia organised the
       <a href="/wiki/2011_IIHF_World_Championship" title="2011 IIHF World Championship">
        2011 IIHF World Championship
       </a>
       in ice hockey, where
       <a href="/wiki/Finland_men%27s_national_ice_hockey_team" title="Finland men's national ice hockey team">
        Finland
       </a>
       won the gold medal. Competitions took place in
       <a href="/wiki/Bratislava" title="Bratislava">
        Bratislava
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ko%C5%A1ice" title="Košice">
        Košice
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Notable Slovak hockey players who played or are still playing in the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">
        NHL
       </a>
       are
       <a href="/wiki/Stan_Mikita" title="Stan Mikita">
        Stan Mikita
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_%C5%A0%C5%A5astn%C3%BD" title="Peter Šťastný">
        Peter Šťastný
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mari%C3%A1n_%C5%A0%C5%A5astn%C3%BD" title="Marián Šťastný">
        Marián Šťastný
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Anton_%C5%A0%C5%A5astn%C3%BD" title="Anton Šťastný">
        Anton Šťastný
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Bondra" title="Peter Bondra">
        Peter Bondra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C5%BDigmund_P%C3%A1lffy" title="Žigmund Pálffy">
        Žigmund Pálffy
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mari%C3%A1n_G%C3%A1bor%C3%ADk" title="Marián Gáborík">
        Marián Gáborík
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mari%C3%A1n_Hossa" title="Marián Hossa">
        Marián Hossa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pavol_Demitra" title="Pavol Demitra">
        Pavol Demitra
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Zdeno_Ch%C3%A1ra" title="Zdeno Chára">
        Zdeno Chára
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Miroslav_%C5%A0atan" title="Miroslav Šatan">
        Miroslav Šatan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C4%BDubom%C3%ADr_Vi%C5%A1%C5%88ovsk%C3%BD" title="Ľubomír Višňovský">
        Ľubomír Višňovský
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tom%C3%A1%C5%A1_Kopeck%C3%BD" title="Tomáš Kopecký">
        Tomáš Kopecký
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Andrej_Sekera" title="Andrej Sekera">
        Andrej Sekera
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jaroslav_Hal%C3%A1k" title="Jaroslav Halák">
        Jaroslav Halák
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dt>
        Football
       </dt>
      </dl>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:CityArena.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="960" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/CityArena.jpg/220px-CityArena.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/CityArena.jpg/330px-CityArena.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/CityArena.jpg/440px-CityArena.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:CityArena.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Football stadium
         <a href="/wiki/%C5%A0tadi%C3%B3n_Antona_Malatinsk%C3%A9ho" title="Štadión Antona Malatinského">
          City Arena
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Trnava" title="Trnava">
          Trnava
         </a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Association football is the most popular sport in Slovakia, with over 400,000 registered players. Since 1993,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovak_national_football_team" title="Slovak national football team">
        Slovak national football team
       </a>
       has qualified only once to the
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">
        FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/2010_FIFA_World_Cup" title="2010 FIFA World Cup">
        2010
       </a>
       , in which they proceeded into the Last 16, where they were defeated by
       <a href="/wiki/Netherlands_national_football_team" title="Netherlands national football team">
        Netherlands
       </a>
       . The most notable result was the 3–2 victory over
       <a href="/wiki/Italy_national_football_team" title="Italy national football team">
        Italy
       </a>
       . In 2016
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slovak_national_football_team" title="Slovak national football team">
        Slovak national football team
       </a>
       has qualified to the
       <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Euro_2016" title="UEFA Euro 2016">
        UEFA Euro 2016
       </a>
       under head coach
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Koz%C3%A1k_(footballer,_born_1954)" title="Ján Kozák (footballer, born 1954)">
        Ján Kozák
       </a>
       which helped the team reach their best ever position of 14th in the
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Rankings" title="FIFA World Rankings">
        FIFA World Rankings
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In club competitions, only three teams have qualified to
       <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Champions_League" title="UEFA Champions League">
        UEFA Champions League
       </a>
       Group Stage, namely
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MFK_Ko%C5%A1ice" title="MFK Košice">
        MFK Košice
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/1997%E2%80%9398_UEFA_Champions_League" title="1997–98 UEFA Champions League">
        1997–98
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/FC_Artmedia_Bratislava" title="FC Artmedia Bratislava">
        FC Artmedia Bratislava
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2005–06 UEFA Champions League">
        2005–06 season
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/M%C5%A0K_%C5%BDilina" title="MŠK Žilina">
        MŠK Žilina
       </a>
       n
       <a href="/wiki/2010%E2%80%9311_UEFA_Champions_League" title="2010–11 UEFA Champions League">
        2010–11
       </a>
       . FC Artmedia Bratislava has been the most successful team after finishing 3rd at the Group Stage, therefore qualifying for the Round of 32 of the
       <a href="/wiki/2005%E2%80%9306_UEFA_Cup" title="2005–06 UEFA Cup">
        UEFA Cup
       </a>
       . They also remain the only Slovak club that has won a match at the group stage.
      </p>
      <p>
       Famous Slovak players include
       <a href="/wiki/Marek_Ham%C5%A1%C3%ADk" title="Marek Hamšík">
        Marek Hamšík
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Martin_%C5%A0krtel" title="Martin Škrtel">
        Martin Škrtel
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Juraj_Kucka" title="Juraj Kucka">
        Juraj Kucka
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Peter_Dubovsk%C3%BD_(footballer)" title="Peter Dubovský (footballer)">
        Peter Dubovský
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Karol_Dobi%C3%A1%C5%A1" title="Karol Dobiáš">
        Karol Dobiáš
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Anton_Ondru%C5%A1" title="Anton Ondruš">
        Anton Ondruš
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mari%C3%A1n_Masn%C3%BD" title="Marián Masný">
        Marián Masný
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_%C5%A0vehl%C3%ADk" title="Ján Švehlík">
        Ján Švehlík
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/J%C3%A1n_Pivarn%C3%ADk" title="Ján Pivarník">
        Ján Pivarník
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jozef_%C4%8Capkovi%C4%8D" title="Jozef Čapkovič">
        Jozef Čapkovič
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Scherer" title="Adolf Scherer">
        Adolf Scherer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Andrej_Kva%C5%A1%C5%88%C3%A1k" title="Andrej Kvašňák">
        Andrej Kvašňák
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Jozef_Adamec" title="Jozef Adamec">
        Jozef Adamec
       </a>
       .
      </p>

       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Slovakia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>

        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">
       <div class="mw-references-wrap">
        <ol class="references">
         <li id="cite_note-22">
          <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
           <b>
            <a href="#cite_ref-22">
             ^
            </a>
           </b>
          </span>
          <span class="reference-text">
           Slovaks differentiate between
           <i>
            Uhorsko
           </i>
           (the historic state) and
           <i>
            Maďarsko
           </i>
           (the modern state) while both tend to be rendered as
           <i>
            Hungary
           </i>
           in English.
          </span>
         </li>
        </ol>

          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Ajournal&amp;rft.genre=article&amp;rft.jtitle=The+Houston+Chronicle&amp;rft.atitle=The+first+%28and+only%29+name+in+jazz+piano&amp;rft.pages=7+section%3A%22ZEST%22&amp;rft.date=2004-12-05&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASlovakia">
           <span style="display:none;">
           </span>
          </span>
         </span>
        </li>
        <li id="cite_note-EuropeNations2000-140">
         <span class="mw-cite-backlink">
          <b>
           <a href="#cite_ref-EuropeNations2000_140-0">
            ^
           </a>
          </b>
         </span>
         <span class="reference-text">
          <cite class="citation book">
           United Nations. Economic Commission for Europe; Food and Agriculture Organization of the United Nations (2000).
           <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Xg_xAAAAMAAJ" rel="nofollow">
            <i>
             Forest resources of Europe, CIS, North America, Australia, Japan and New Zealand (industrialised temperate/boreal countries): UN-ECE/FAO contribution to the Global Forest Resources Assessment 2000
            </i>
           </a>
           . United Nations. pp. 347–.
           <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">
            ISBN
           </a>
           <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/978-92-1-116735-1" title="Special:BookSources/978-92-1-116735-1">
            978-92-1-116735-1
           </a>
           .
           <q>
            In some countries, the commercial sale of game meat is an important economic activity, including the export of game meat. ... value in the Netherlands, and as the value of export, domestic consumption, and industrial processing in Slovakia.
           </q>
          </cite>
          <span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=Forest+resources+of+Europe%2C+CIS%2C+North+America%2C+Australia%2C+Japan+and+New+Zealand+%28industrialised+temperate%2Fboreal+countries%29%3A+UN-ECE%2FFAO+contribution+to+the+Global+Forest+Resources+Assessment+2000&amp;rft.pages=347-&amp;rft.pub=United+Nations&amp;rft.date=2000&amp;rft.isbn=978-92-1-116735-1&amp;rft.au=United+Nations.+Economic+Commission+for+Europe&amp;rft.au=Food+and+Agriculture+Organization+of+the+United+Nations&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DXg_xAAAAMAAJ&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ASlovakia">

              <td class="navbox-abovebelow" colspan="3" style="text-align:left;">
               <div>
                <div class="plainlist">
                 <ul>
                  <li>
                   <sup>
                    1
                   </sup>
                   <a href="/wiki/Island#Oceanic_islands" title="Island">
                    Oceanic islands
                   </a>
                   within the vicinity of Europe are usually grouped with the continent even though they are not situated on its continental shelf.
                  </li>
                  <li>
                   <sup>
                    2
                   </sup>
                   Some countries completely outside the conventional geographical boundaries of Europe are commonly associated with the continent due to ethnological links.
                  </li>
                 </ul>
